10123{_}924{_}queried Louise, evidently amused.
10123{_}925{_}"It's plain to me that Aunt Jane has invited us here to choose which one of us shall inherit her money--and Elmhurst.
10123{_}926{_}She's old and feeble, and she hasn't any other relations."
10123{_}927{_}"Oh, yes, she has" corrected Louise.
10123{_}928{_}"You mean Patricia Doyle?"
10123{_}929{_}"Yes."
10123{_}930{_}"What do you know of her?"
10123{_}931{_}"Nothing at all."
10123{_}932{_}"Where does she live?"
10123{_}933{_}"I haven't the faintest idea."
10123{_}934{_}Louise spoke as calmly as if she had not mailed Patricia's defiant letter to Aunt Jane, or discovered her cousin's identity in the little hair-dresser from Madame Borne's establishment.
10123{_}935{_}"Has Aunt Jane mentioned her?"
10123{_}936{_}continued Beth.
10123{_}937{_}"Not in my presence."
10123{_}938{_}"Then we may conclude she's left out of the arrangement," said Beth, calmly.
10123{_}939{_}"And, as I said, Aunt Jane is likely to choose one of us to succeed her at Elmhurst.
10123{_}940{_}I hoped I had it all my own way, but it's evident I was mistaken.
10123{_}941{_}You'll fight for your chance and fight mighty hard!"
10123{_}942{_}Louise laughed merrily.
10123{_}943{_}"How funny!"
10123{_}944{_}she exclaimed, after a moment during which Beth frowned at her darkly.
10123{_}945{_}"Why, my dear cousin, I don't want Aunt Jane's money."
10123{_}946{_}"You don't?"
10123{_}947{_}"Not a penny of it; nor Elmhurst; nor anything you can possibly lay claim to, my dear.
10123{_}948{_}My mother and I are amply provided for, and I am only here to find rest from my social duties and to get acquainted with my dead father's sister.
10123{_}949{_}That is all."
10123{_}950{_}"Oh!"
10123{_}951{_}said Beth, lying back in her chair with a sigh of relief.
10123{_}952{_}"So it was really a splendid idea of yours to be frank with me at our first meeting," continued Louise, cheerfully; "for it has led to your learning the truth, and I am sure you will never again grieve me by suggesting that I wish to supplant you in Aunt Jane's favor.
10123{_}953{_}Now tell me something about yourself and your people.
10123{_}954{_}Are you poor?"
10123{_}955{_}"Poor as poverty," said Beth, gloomily.
10123{_}956{_}"My father teaches music, and mother scolds him continually for not being able to earn enough money to keep out of debt."
10123{_}957{_}"Hasn't Aunt Jane helped you?"
10123{_}958{_}"We've never seen a cent of her money, although father has tried at times to borrow enough to help him out of his difficulties."
10123{_}959{_}"That's strange.
10123{_}960{_}She seems like such a dear kindly old lady," said Louise, musingly.
10123{_}961{_}"I think she's horrid," answered Beth, angrily; "but I mustn't let her know it.
10123{_}962{_}I even kissed her, when she asked me to, and it sent a shiver all down my back."
10123{_}963{_}Louise laughed with genuine amusement.
10123{_}964{_}"You must dissemble, Cousin Elizabeth," she advised, "and teach our aunt to love you.
10123{_}965{_}For my part, I am fond of everyone, and it delights me to fuss around invalids and assist them.
10123{_}966{_}I ought to have been a trained nurse, you know; but of course there's no necessity of my earning a living."
10123{_}967{_}"I suppose not," said Beth.
10123{_}968{_}Then, after a thoughtful silence, she resumed abruptly; "What's to prevent Aunt Jane leaving you her property, even if you are rich, and don't need it?
10123{_}969{_}You say you like to care for invalids, and I don't.
10123{_}970{_}Suppose Aunt Jane prefers you to me, and wills you all her money?"
10123{_}971{_}"Why, that would be beyond my power to prevent," answered Louise, with a little yawn.
10123{_}972{_}Beth's face grew hard again.
10123{_}973{_}"You're deceiving me," she declared, angrily.
10123{_}974{_}"You're trying to make me think you don't want Elmhurst, when you're as anxious to get it as I am."
10123{_}975{_}"My dear Elizabeth--by the way, that's an awfully long name; what do they call you, Lizzie, or Bessie, or--"  "They call me Beth," sullenly.
10123{_}976{_}"Then, my dear Beth, let me beg you not to borrow trouble, or to doubt one who wishes to be your friend.
10123{_}977{_}Elmhurst would be a perfect bore to me.
10123{_}978{_}I wouldn't know what to do with it.
10123{_}979{_}I couldn't live in this out-of-the-way corner of the world, you know."
10123{_}980{_}"But suppose she leaves it to you?"
10123{_}981{_}persisted Beth.
10123{_}982{_}"You wouldn't refuse it, I imagine."
10123{_}983{_}Louise seemed to meditate.
10123{_}984{_}"Cousin," she said, at length, "I'll make a bargain with you.
10123{_}985{_}I can't refuse to love and pet Aunt Jane, just because she has money and my sweet cousin Beth is anxious to inherit it.
10123{_}986{_}But I'll not interfere in any way with your chances, and I'll promise to sing your praises to our aunt persistently.
10123{_}987{_}Furthermore, in case she selects me as her heir, I will agree to transfer half of the estate to you--the half that consists of Elmhurst."
10123{_}988{_}"Is there much more?"
10123{_}989{_}asked Beth.
10123{_}990{_}"I haven't any list of Aunt Jane's possessions, so I don't know.
10123{_}991{_}But you shall have Elmhurst, if I get it, because the place would be of no use to me."
10123{_}992{_}"It's a magnificent estate," said Beth, looking at her cousin doubtfully.
10123{_}993{_}"It shall be yours, dear, whatever Aunt Jane decides.
10123{_}994{_}See, this is a compact, and I'll seal it with a kiss."
10123{_}995{_}She sprang up and, kneeling beside Beth, kissed her fervently.
10123{_}996{_}"Now shall we be friends?"
10123{_}997{_}she asked, lightly.
10123{_}998{_}"Now will you abandon all those naughty suspicions and let me love you?"
10123{_}999{_}Beth hesitated.
10123{_}1000{_}The suggestion seemed preposterous.
10123{_}1001{_}Such generosity savored of play acting, and Louise's manner was too airy to be genuine.
10123{_}1002{_}Somehow she felt that she was being laughed at by this slender, graceful girl, who was scarcely older than herself; but she was too unsophisticated to know how to resent it.
10123{_}1003{_}Louise insisted upon warding off her enmity, or at least establishing a truce, and Beth, however suspicious and ungracious, could find no way of rejecting the overtures.
10123{_}1004{_}"Were I in your place," she said, "I would never promise to give up a penny of the inheritance.
10123{_}1005{_}If I win it, I shall keep it all."
10123{_}1006{_}"To be sure.
10123{_}1007{_}I should want you to, my dear."
10123{_}1008{_}"Then, since we have no cause to quarrel, we may as well become friends," continued Beth, her features relaxing a little their set expression.
10123{_}1009{_}Louise laughed again, ignoring the other's brusqueness, and was soon chatting away pleasantly upon other subjects and striving to draw Beth out of her natural reserve.
10123{_}1010{_}The younger girl had no power to resist such fascinations.
10123{_}1011{_}Louise knew the big world, and talked of it with charming naivete, and Beth listened rapturously.
10123{_}1012{_}Such a girl friend it had never been her privilege to have before, and when her suspicions were forgotten she became fairly responsive, and brightened wonderfully.
10123{_}1013{_}They dressed in time for dinner, and met Aunt Jane and Silas Watson, the lawyer, in the great drawing-room.
10123{_}1014{_}The old gentleman was very attentive and courteous during the stately dinner, and did much to relieve the girls' embarrassment.
10123{_}1015{_}Louise, indeed, seemed quite at home in her new surroundings, and chatted most vivaciously during the meal; but Aunt Jane was strangely silent, and Beth had little to say and seemed awkward and ill at ease.
10123{_}1016{_}The old lady retired to her own room shortly after dinner, and presently sent a servant to request Mr. Watson to join her.
10123{_}1017{_}"Silas," she said, when he entered, "what do you think of my nieces?"
10123{_}1018{_}"They are very charming girls," he answered, "although they are at an age when few girls show to good advantage.
10123{_}1019{_}Why did you not invite Kenneth to dinner, Jane?"
10123{_}1020{_}"The boy?"
10123{_}1021{_}"Yes.
10123{_}1022{_}They would be more at ease in the society of a young gentleman more nearly their own age."
10123{_}1023{_}"Kenneth is a bear.
10123{_}1024{_}He is constantly saying disagreeable things.
10123{_}1025{_}In other words, he is not gentlemanly, and the girls shall have nothing to do with him."
10123{_}1026{_}"Very well," said the lawyer, quietly.
10123{_}1027{_}"Which of my nieces do you prefer?"
10123{_}1028{_}asked the old lady, after a pause.
10123{_}1029{_}"I cannot say, on so short an acquaintance," he answered, with gravity.
10123{_}1030{_}"Which do you prefer, Jane?"
10123{_}1031{_}"They are equally unsatisfactory," she answered.
10123{_}1032{_}"I cannot imagine Elmhurst belonging to either, Silas."
10123{_}1033{_}Then she added, with an abrupt change of manner: "You must go to New York for me, at once."
10123{_}1034{_}"Tonight?"
10123{_}1035{_}"No; tomorrow morning.
10123{_}1036{_}I must see that other niece--the one who defies me and refuses to answer my second letter."
10123{_}1037{_}"Patricia Doyle?"
10123{_}1038{_}"Yes.
10123{_}1039{_}Find her and argue with her.
10123{_}1040{_}Tell her I am a crabbed old woman with a whim to know her, and that I shall not die happy unless she comes to Elmhurst.
10123{_}1041{_}Bribe her, threaten her--kidnap her if necessary, Silas; but get her to Elmhurst as quickly as possible."
10123{_}1042{_}"I'll do my best, Jane.
10123{_}1043{_}But why are you so anxious?"
10123{_}1044{_}"My time is drawing near, old friend," she replied, less harshly than usual, "and this matter of my will lies heavily on my conscience.
10123{_}1045{_}What if I should die tonight?"
10123{_}1046{_}He did not answer.
10123{_}1047{_}"There would be a dozen heirs to fight for my money, and dear old Elmhurst would be sold to strangers," she resumed, with bitterness.
10123{_}1048{_}"But I don't mean to cross over just yet, Silas, even if one limb is dead already.
10123{_}1049{_}I shall hang on until I get this matter settled, and I can't settle it properly without seeing all three of my nieces.
10123{_}1050{_}One of these is too hard, and the other too soft.
10123{_}1051{_}I'll see what Patricia is like."
10123{_}1052{_}"She may prove even more undesirable," said the lawyer.
10123{_}1053{_}"In that case, I'll pack her back again and choose between these two.
10123{_}1054{_}But you must fetch her, Silas, that I may know just what I am doing.
10123{_}1055{_}And you must fetch her at once!"
10123{_}1056{_}"I'll do the best I can, Jane," repeated the old lawyer.
10123{_}1057{_}CHAPTER X.
10123{_}1058{_}THE MAN WITH THE BUNDLE.
10123{_}1059{_}In the harness-room above the stable sat Duncan Muir, the coachman and most important servant, with the exception of the head gardener, in Miss Merrick's establishment.
10123{_}1060{_}Duncan, bald-headed but with white and bushy side-whiskers, was engaged in the serious business of oiling and polishing the state harness, which had not been used for many months past.
10123{_}1061{_}But that did not matter.
10123{_}1062{_}Thursday was the day for oiling the harness, and so on Thursday he performed the task, never daring to entrust a work so important to a subordinate.
10123{_}1063{_}In one corner of the little room Kenneth Forbes squatted upon a bench, with an empty pine box held carelessly in his lap.
10123{_}1064{_}While Duncan worked the boy was busy with his pencil, but neither had spoken for at least a half hour.
10123{_}1065{_}Finally the aged coachman, without looking up, enquired:  "What do ye think o' 'em, Kenneth lad?"
10123{_}1066{_}"Think o' whom, Don?"
10123{_}1067{_}"The young leddies."
10123{_}1068{_}"What young ladies?"
10123{_}1069{_}"Miss Jane's nieces, as Oscar brought from the station yesterday."
10123{_}1070{_}The boy looked astonished, and leaned over the box in his lap eagerly.
10123{_}1071{_}"Tell me, Don," he said.
10123{_}1072{_}"I was away with my gun all yesterday, and heard nothing of it."
10123{_}1073{_}"Why, it seems Miss Jane's invited 'em to make her a visit."
10123{_}1074{_}"But not yet, Don!
10123{_}1075{_}Not so soon."
10123{_}1076{_}"Na'theless, they're here."
10123{_}1077{_}"How many, Don?"
10123{_}1078{_}"Two, lad.
10123{_}1079{_}A bonny young thing came on the morning train, an' a nice, wide-awake one by the two o'clock."
10123{_}1080{_}"Girls?"
10123{_}1081{_}with an accent of horror.
10123{_}1082{_}"Young females, anyhow," said Donald, polishing a buckle briskly.
10123{_}1083{_}The boy glared at him fixedly.
10123{_}1084{_}"Will they be running about the place, Don?"
10123{_}1085{_}"Most likely, 'Twould be a shame to shut them up with the poor missus this glad weather.
10123{_}1086{_}But why not?
10123{_}1087{_}They'll be company for ye, Kenneth lad."
10123{_}1088{_}"How long will they stay?"
10123{_}1089{_}"Mabbe for aye.
10123{_}1090{_}Oscar forbys one or the ither o' 'em will own the place when Miss Jane gi'es up the ghost."
10123{_}1091{_}The boy sat silent a moment, thinking upon this speech.
10123{_}1092{_}Then, with a cry that was almost a scream, he dashed the box upon the floor and flew out the door as if crazed, and Donald paused to listen to his footsteps clattering down the stairs.
10123{_}1093{_}Then the old man groaned dismally, shaking his side-whiskers with a negative expression that might have conveyed worlds of meaning to one able to interpret it.
10123{_}1094{_}But his eye fell upon the pine box, which had rolled to his feet, and he stooped to pick it up.
10123{_}1095{_}Upon the smoothly planed side was his own picture, most deftly drawn, showing him engaged in polishing the harness.
10123{_}1096{_}Every strap and buckle was depicted with rare fidelity; there was no doubt at all of the sponge and bottle on the stool beside him, or the cloth in his hand.
10123{_}1097{_}Even his bow spectacles rested upon the bridge of his nose at exactly the right angle, and his under lip protruded just as it had done since he was a lad.
10123{_}1098{_}Donald was not only deeply impressed by such an exhibition of art; he was highly gratified at being pictured, and full of wonder that the boy could do such a thing; "wi' a wee pencil an' a bit o' board!"
10123{_}1099{_}He turned the box this way and that to admire the sketch, and finally arose and brought a hatchet, with which he carefully pried the board away from the box.
10123{_}1100{_}Then he carried his treasure to a cupboard, where he hid it safely behind a row of tall bottles.
10123{_}1101{_}Meantime Kenneth had reached the stable, thrown a bridle over the head of a fine sorrel mare, and scorning to use a saddle leaped upon her back and dashed down the lane and out at the rear gate upon the old turnpike road.
10123{_}1102{_}His head was whirling with amazement, his heart full of indignation.
10123{_}1103{_}Girls!
10123{_}1104{_}Girls at Elmhurst--nieces and guests of the fierce old woman he so bitterly hated!
10123{_}1105{_}Then, indeed, his days of peace and quiet were ended.
10123{_}1106{_}These dreadful creatures would prowl around everywhere; they might even penetrate the shrubbery to the foot of the stairs leading to his own retired room; they would destroy his happiness and drive him mad.
10123{_}1107{_}For this moody, silent youth had been strangely happy in his life at Elmhurst, despite the neglect of the grim old woman who was its mistress and the fact that no one aside from Lawyer Watson seemed to care whether he lived or died.
10123{_}1108{_}Perhaps Donald did.
10123{_}1109{_}Good old Don was friendly and seldom bothered him by talking.
10123{_}1110{_}Perhaps old Misery liked him a bit, also.
10123{_}1111{_}But these were only servants, and almost as helpless and dependent as himself.
10123{_}1112{_}Still, he had been happy.
10123{_}1113{_}He began to realize it, now that these awful girls had come to disturb his peace.
10123{_}1114{_}The thought filled him with grief and rebellion and resentment; yet there was nothing he could do to alter the fact that Donald's "young females" were already here, and prepared, doubtless, to stay.
10123{_}1115{_}The sorrel was dashing down the road at a great pace, but the boy clung firmly to his seat and gloried in the breeze that fanned his hot cheeks.
10123{_}1116{_}Away and away he raced until he reached the crossroads, miles away, and down this he turned and galloped as recklessly as before.
10123{_}1117{_}The sun was hot, today, and the sorrel's flanks begun to steam and show flecks of white upon their glossy surface.
10123{_}1118{_}He turned again to the left, entering upon a broad highway that would lead him straight home at last; but he had almost reached the little village of Elmwood, which was the railway station, before he realized his cruelty to the splendid mare he bestrode.
10123{_}1119{_}Then indeed, he fell to a walk, patting Nora's neck affectionately and begging her to forgive him for his thoughtlessness.
10123{_}1120{_}The mare tossed her head in derision.
10123{_}1121{_}However she might sweat and pant, she liked the glorious pace even better than her rider.
10123{_}1122{_}Through the village he paced moodily, the bridle dangling loosely on the mare's neck.
10123{_}1123{_}The people paused to look at him curiously, but he had neither word nor look for any.
10123{_}1124{_}He did not know one of them by name, and cared little how much they might speculate upon his peculiar position at "the big house."
10123{_}1125{_}Then, riding slowly up the hedge bordered road, his troubles once more assailed him, and he wondered if there was not some spot upon the broad earth to which he could fly for retirement until the girls had left Elmhurst for good.
10123{_}1126{_}Nora shied, and he looked up to discover that he had nearly run down a pedestrian--a stout little man with a bundle under his arm, who held up one hand as if to arrest him.
10123{_}1127{_}Involuntarily he drew rein, and stopped beside the traveler with a look of inquiry.
10123{_}1128{_}"Sorry to trouble you, sir," remarked the little man, in a cheery voice, "but I ain't just certain about my way."
10123{_}1129{_}"Where do you want to go?"
10123{_}1130{_}asked the boy.
10123{_}1131{_}"To Jane Merrick's place.
10123{_}1132{_}They call it Elmhurst, I guess."
10123{_}1133{_}"It's straight ahead," said Kenneth, as the mare walked on.
10123{_}1134{_}His questioner also started and paced beside him.
10123{_}1135{_}"Far from here?"
10123{_}1136{_}"A mile, perhaps."
10123{_}1137{_}"They said it was three from the village, but I guess I've come a dozen a'ready."
10123{_}1138{_}The boy did not reply to this.
10123{_}1139{_}There was nothing offensive in the man's manner.
10123{_}1140{_}He spoke with an easy familiarity that made it difficult not to respond with equal frank cordiality, and there was a shrewd expression upon his wrinkled, smooth-shaven face that stamped him a man who had seen life in many of its phases.
10123{_}1141{_}Kenneth, who resented the companionship of most people, seemed attracted by the man, and hesitated to gallop on and leave him.
10123{_}1142{_}"Know Jane Merrick?"
10123{_}1143{_}asked the stranger.
10123{_}1144{_}The boy nodded.
10123{_}1145{_}"Like her?"
10123{_}1146{_}"I hate her," he said, savagely.
10123{_}1147{_}The man laughed, a bit uneasily.
10123{_}1148{_}"Then it's the same Jane as ever," he responded, with a shake of his grizzled head.
10123{_}1149{_}"Do you know, I sort o' hoped she'd reformed, and I'd be glad to see her again.
10123{_}1150{_}They tell me she's got money."
10123{_}1151{_}The boy looked at him in surprise.
10123{_}1152{_}"She owns Elmhurst, and has mortgages on a dozen farms around here, and property in New York, and thousands of dollars in the bank," he said.
10123{_}1153{_}"Aunt Jane's rich."
10123{_}1154{_}"Aunt Jane?"
10123{_}1155{_}echoed the man, quickly.
10123{_}1156{_}"What's your name, lad?"
10123{_}1157{_}"Kenneth Forbes."
10123{_}1158{_}A shake of the head.
10123{_}1159{_}"Don't recollect any Forbeses in the family."
10123{_}1160{_}"She isn't really my aunt," said the boy, "and she doesn't treat me as an aunt, either; but she's my guardian, and I've always called her Aunt, rather than say Miss Merrick."
10123{_}1161{_}"She's never married, has she?"
10123{_}1162{_}"No.
10123{_}1163{_}She was engaged to my Uncle Tom, who owned Elmhurst.
10123{_}1164{_}He was killed in a railway accident, and then it was found he'd left her all he had."
10123{_}1165{_}"I see."
10123{_}1166{_}"So, when my parents died, Aunt Jane took me for Uncle Tom's sake, and keeps me out of charity."
10123{_}1167{_}"I see."
10123{_}1168{_}Quite soberly, this time.
10123{_}1169{_}The boy slid off the mare and walked beside the little man, holding the bridle over his arm.
10123{_}1170{_}They did not speak again for some moments.
10123{_}1171{_}Finally the stranger asked:  "Are Jane's sisters living--Julia and Violet?"
10123{_}1172{_}"I don't know.
10123{_}1173{_}But there are two of her nieces at Elmhurst."
10123{_}1174{_}"Ha!
10123{_}1175{_}Who are they?"
10123{_}1176{_}"Girls," with bitterness.
10123{_}1177{_}"I haven't seen them."
10123{_}1178{_}The stranger whistled.
10123{_}1179{_}"Don't like girls, I take it?"
10123{_}1180{_}"No; I hate them."
10123{_}1181{_}Another long pause.
10123{_}1182{_}Then the boy suddenly turned questioner.
10123{_}1183{_}"You know Aunt--Miss Merrick, sir?"
10123{_}1184{_}"I used to, when we were both younger."
10123{_}1185{_}"Any relation, sir?"
10123{_}1186{_}"Just a brother, that's all."
10123{_}1187{_}Kenneth stopped short, and the mare stopped, and the little man, with a whimsical smile at the boy's astonishment, also stopped.
10123{_}1188{_}"I didn't know she had a brother, sir--that is, living."
10123{_}1189{_}"She had two; but Will's dead, years ago, I'm told.
10123{_}1190{_}I'm the other."
10123{_}1191{_}"John Merrick?"
10123{_}1192{_}"That's me.
10123{_}1193{_}I went west a long time ago; before you were born, I guess.
10123{_}1194{_}We don't get much news on the coast, so I sort of lost track of the folks back east, and I reckon they lost track of me, for the same reason."
10123{_}1195{_}"You were the tinsmith?"
10123{_}1196{_}"The same.
10123{_}1197{_}Bad pennies always return, they say.
10123{_}1198{_}I've come back to look up the family and find how many are left.
10123{_}1199{_}Curious sort of a job, isn't it."
10123{_}1200{_}"I don't know.
10123{_}1201{_}Perhaps it's natural," replied the boy, reflectively.
10123{_}1202{_}"But I'm sorry you came to Aunt Jane first."
10123{_}1203{_}"Why?"
10123{_}1204{_}"She's in bad health--quite ill, you know--and her temper's dreadful.
10123{_}1205{_}Perhaps she--she--"  "I know.
10123{_}1206{_}But I haven't seen her in years; and, after all, she's my sister.
10123{_}1207{_}And back at the old home, where I went first, no one knew anything about what had become of the family except Jane.
10123{_}1208{_}They kept track of her because she suddenly became rich, and a great lady, and that was a surprising thing to happen to a Merrick.
10123{_}1209{_}We've always been a poor lot, you know."
10123{_}1210{_}The boy glanced at the bundle, pityingly, and the little man caught the look and smiled his sweet, cheery smile.
10123{_}1211{_}"My valise was too heavy to carry," he said; "so I wrapped up a few things in case Jane wanted me to stay over night.
10123{_}1212{_}And that's why I didn't get a horse at the livery, you know.
10123{_}1213{_}Somebody'd have to take it back again."
10123{_}1214{_}"I'm sure she'll ask you to stay, sir.
10123{_}1215{_}And if she doesn't, you come out to the stable and let me know, and I'll drive you to town again.
10123{_}1216{_}Donald--that's the coachman--is my friend, and he'll let me have the horse if I ask him."
10123{_}1217{_}"Thank you, lad," returned the man, gratefully.
10123{_}1218{_}"I thought a little exercise would do me good, but this three miles has seemed like thirty to me!"
10123{_}1219{_}"We're here at last," said the boy, turning: into the drive-way.
10123{_}1220{_}"Seeing that you're her brother, sir, I advise you to go right up to the front door and ring the bell."
10123{_}1221{_}"I will," said the man.
10123{_}1222{_}"I always go around the back way, myself."
10123{_}1223{_}"I see."
10123{_}1224{_}The boy turned away, but in a moment halted again.
10123{_}1225{_}His interest in Miss Jane's brother John was extraordinary.
10123{_}1226{_}"Another thing," he said, hesitating.
10123{_}1227{_}"Well?"
10123{_}1228{_}"You'd better not say you met me, you know.
10123{_}1229{_}It wouldn't be a good introduction.
10123{_}1230{_}She hates me as much as I hate her."
10123{_}1231{_}"Very good, my lad.
10123{_}1232{_}I'll keep mum."
10123{_}1233{_}The boy nodded, and turned away to lead Nora to the stable.
10123{_}1234{_}The man looked after him a moment, and shook his head, sadly.
10123{_}1235{_}"Poor boy!"
10123{_}1236{_}he whispered.
10123{_}1237{_}Then he walked up to the front door and rang the bell.
10123{_}1238{_}CHAPTER XI.
10123{_}1239{_}THE MAD GARDENER.
10123{_}1240{_}"This seems to be a lazy place," said Louise, as she stood in the doorway of Beth's room to bid her good night.
10123{_}1241{_}"I shall sleep until late in the morning, for I don't believe Aunt Jane will be on exhibition before noon."
10123{_}1242{_}"At home I always get up at six o'clock," answered Beth.
10123{_}1243{_}"Six o'clock!
10123{_}1244{_}Good gracious!
10123{_}1245{_}What for?"
10123{_}1246{_}"To study my lessons and help get the breakfast."
10123{_}1247{_}"Don't you keep a maid?"
10123{_}1248{_}"No," said Beth, rather surlily; "we have hard work to keep ourselves."
10123{_}1249{_}"But you must be nearly through with school by this time.
10123{_}1250{_}I finished my education ages ago."
10123{_}1251{_}"Did you graduate?"
10123{_}1252{_}asked Beth.
10123{_}1253{_}"No; it wasn't worth while," declared Louise, complacently.
10123{_}1254{_}"I'm sure I know as much as most girls do, and there are more useful lessons to be learned from real life than from books."
10123{_}1255{_}"Good night," said Beth.
10123{_}1256{_}"Good night," answered the older girl, and shut the door behind her.
10123{_}1257{_}Beth sat for a time moodily thinking.
10123{_}1258{_}She did not like the way in which her cousin assumed superiority over her.
10123{_}1259{_}The difference in their ages did not account for the greater worldly wisdom Louise had acquired, and in much that she said and did Beth recognized a shrewdness and experience that made her feel humbled and, in a way, inferior to her cousin.
10123{_}1260{_}Nor did she trust the friendship Louise expressed for her.
10123{_}1261{_}Somehow, nothing that the girl said seemed to ring true, and Beth already, in her mind, accused her of treachery and insincerity.
10123{_}1262{_}As a matter of fact, however, she failed to understand her cousin.
10123{_}1263{_}Louise really loved to be nice to people, and to say nice thing's.
10123{_}1264{_}It is true she schemed and intrigued to advance her personal welfare and position in life; but even her schemes were undertaken lightly and carelessly, and if they failed the girl would be the first to laugh at her disappointment and try to mend her fortunes.
10123{_}1265{_}If others stood in her way she might not consider them at all; if she pledged her word, it might not always be profitable to keep it; but she liked to be on pleasant terms with everyone, and would be amiable to the last, no matter what happened.
10123{_}1266{_}Comedy was her forte, rather than tragedy.
10123{_}1267{_}If tragedy entered her life she would probably turn it into ridicule.
10123{_}1268{_}Wholly without care, whimsical and generous to a degree, if it suited her mood, Louise Merrick possessed a nature capable of great things, either for good or ill.
10123{_}1269{_}It was no wonder her unsophisticated country cousin failed to comprehend her, although Beth's intuition was not greatly at fault.
10123{_}1270{_}Six o'clock found Beth wide awake, as usual; so she quietly dressed and, taking her book under her arm, started to make her way into the gardens.
10123{_}1271{_}Despite Louise's cynicism she had no intention of abandoning her studies.
10123{_}1272{_}She had decided to fit herself for a teacher before Aunt Jane's invitation had come to her, and this ambition would render it necessary for her to study hard during vacations.
10123{_}1273{_}If she became an heiress she would not need to teach, but she was not at all confident of her prospects, and the girl's practical nature prompted her to carry out her plans until she was sure of the future.
10123{_}1274{_}In the hall she met Phibbs, shuffling along as if in pain.
10123{_}1275{_}"Good morning, miss," said the old servant.
10123{_}1276{_}Beth looked at her thoughtfully.
10123{_}1277{_}This was Aunt Jane's special and confidential attendant.
10123{_}1278{_}"Do your feet hurt you?"
10123{_}1279{_}she asked.
10123{_}1280{_}"Yes, miss; in the mornin' they's awful bad.
10123{_}1281{_}It's being on 'em all the day, 'tendin' to Miss Jane, you know.
10123{_}1282{_}But after a time I gets more used to the pain, and don't feel it.
10123{_}1283{_}The mornin's always the worst."
10123{_}1284{_}She was passing on, but Beth stopped her.
10123{_}1285{_}"Come into my room," she said, and led the way.
10123{_}1286{_}Martha Phibbs followed reluctantly.
10123{_}1287{_}Miss Jane might already be awake and demanding her services, and she could not imagine what the young lady wanted her for.
10123{_}1288{_}But she entered the room, and Beth went to a box and brought out a bottle of lotion.
10123{_}1289{_}"Mother has the same trouble that you complain of," she said, practically, "and here is a remedy that always gives her relief.
10123{_}1290{_}I brought it with me in case I should take long tramps, and get sore feet."
10123{_}1291{_}She gently pushed the old woman into a chair, and then, to Phibbs' utter amazement, knelt down and unfastened her shoes and drew off her stockings.
10123{_}1292{_}A moment later she was rubbing the lotion upon the poor creature's swollen feet, paying no attention to Martha's horrified protests.
10123{_}1293{_}"There.
10123{_}1294{_}Now they're sure to feel better," said Beth, pulling the worn and darned stockings upon the woman's feet again.
10123{_}1295{_}"And you must take this bottle to your room, and use it every night and morning."
10123{_}1296{_}"Bless your dear heart!"
10123{_}1297{_}cried Phibbs, while tears of gratitude stood in her faded eyes.
10123{_}1298{_}"I'm sure I feel twenty years younger, a'ready.
10123{_}1299{_}But you shouldn't 'a' done it, miss; indeed you shouldn't."
10123{_}1300{_}"I'm glad to help you," said Beth, rinsing her hands at the wash stand and drying them upon a towel.
10123{_}1301{_}"It would be cruel to let you suffer when I can ease your pain."
10123{_}1302{_}"But what would Miss Jane say?"
10123{_}1303{_}wailed old Martha, throwing up her hands in dismay.
10123{_}1304{_}"She'll never know a thing about it.
10123{_}1305{_}It's our secret, Martha, and I'm sure if I ever need a friend you'll do as much for me."
10123{_}1306{_}"I'll do anything for you, Miss Elizabeth," was the reply, as the woman took the bottle of lotion and departed.
10123{_}1307{_}Beth smiled.
10123{_}1308{_}"That was not a bad thought," she said to herself, again starting for the gardens.
10123{_}1309{_}"I have made a firm friend and done a kindly action at the same time--and all while Cousin Louise is fast asleep."
10123{_}1310{_}The housekeeper let her out at the side door, after Beth had pressed her hand and kissed her good morning.
10123{_}1311{_}"You're looking quite bonny, my dear," said the old woman.
10123{_}1312{_}"Do you feel at home, at all, in this strange place?"
10123{_}1313{_}"Not quite, as yet," answered Beth.
10123{_}1314{_}"But I know I have one good friend here, and that comforts me."
10123{_}1315{_}She found a path between high hedges, that wandered away through the grounds, and along this she strolled until she reached a rose arbor with a comfortable bench.
10123{_}1316{_}Here she seated herself, looking around her curiously.
10123{_}1317{_}The place seemed little frequented, but was kept with scrupulous care.
10123{_}1318{_}Even at this hour, a little way off could be heard the "click-click!"
10123{_}1319{_}of hedge-shears, and Beth noted how neatly the paths were swept, and how carefully every rose on the arbor was protected.
10123{_}1320{_}Elmhurst was a beautiful place.
10123{_}1321{_}Beth sighed as she wondered if it would ever be hers.
10123{_}1322{_}Then she opened her book and began to work.
10123{_}1323{_}During the next hour the click of the hedge-shears drew nearer, but the girl did not notice this.
10123{_}1324{_}In another half hour James himself came into view, intent upon his monotonous task.
10123{_}1325{_}Gradually the motionless form of the girl and the plodding figure of the gardener drew together, until he stood but two yards distant.
10123{_}1326{_}Then he paused, looked toward the arbor, and uttered an exclamation.
10123{_}1327{_}Beth looked up.
10123{_}1328{_}"Good morning," she said, pleasantly.
10123{_}1329{_}James stared at her, but made no reply save a slight inclination of his head.
10123{_}1330{_}"Am I in your way?"
10123{_}1331{_}she asked.
10123{_}1332{_}He turned his back to her, then, and began clipping away as before.
10123{_}1333{_}Beth sprang up and laid a hand upon his arm, arresting him.
10123{_}1334{_}Again he turned to stare at her, and in his eyes was a look almost of fear.
10123{_}1335{_}She drew back.
10123{_}1336{_}"Why won't you speak to me?"
10123{_}1337{_}enquired the girl, gently.
10123{_}1338{_}"I'm a stranger at Elmhurst, but I want to be your friend.
10123{_}1339{_}Won't you let me?"
10123{_}1340{_}To her amazement James threw up his hands, letting the shears clatter to the ground, and with a hoarse cry turned and fled up the path as swiftly as he could go.
10123{_}1341{_}Beth was really puzzled, but as she stood silently looking after the gardener she heard a soft laugh, and found old Misery beside her.
10123{_}1342{_}"It's just his way, Miss; don't you be scared by anything that James does," said the woman.
10123{_}1343{_}"Why, at times he won't even speak to Miss Jane."
10123{_}1344{_}"He isn't dumb, is he?"
10123{_}1345{_}asked Beth.
10123{_}1346{_}"Lor', no!
10123{_}1347{_}But he's that odd an' contrary he won't talk to a soul.
10123{_}1348{_}Never did, since the day Master Tom was killed.
10123{_}1349{_}James was travellin' with Master Tom, you know, and there was an accident, an' the train run off'n the track an' tipped over.
10123{_}1350{_}James wasn't hurt at all, but he dragged Master Tom out'n the wreck and sat by him until he died.
10123{_}1351{_}Then James brought Master Tom's body back home again; but his mind seemed to have got a shock, in some way, and he never was the same afterwards.
10123{_}1352{_}He was powerful fond of young Master Tom.
10123{_}1353{_}But then, we all was."
10123{_}1354{_}"Poor man!"
10123{_}1355{_}said Beth.
10123{_}1356{_}"After that," resumed Misery, "all that James would do was to look after the flowers.
10123{_}1357{_}Miss Jane, after she came, made him the head gardener, and he's proved a rare good one, too.
10123{_}1358{_}But James he won't even talk to Miss Jane, nor even to his old friend Lawyer Watson, who used to be Master Tom's special chum an' comrade.
10123{_}1359{_}He does his duty, and obeys all Miss Jane's orders as faithful as can be; but he won't talk, an' we've all give up tryin' to make him."
10123{_}1360{_}"But why should I frighten him?"
10123{_}1361{_}asked the girl.
10123{_}1362{_}"You tried to make him talk, and you're a stranger.
10123{_}1363{_}Strangers always affect James that way.
10123{_}1364{_}I remember when Miss Jane first came to Elmhurst he screamed at the sight of her; but when he found out that Master Tom loved her and had given her Elmhurst, James followed her around like a dog, and did everything she told him to.
10123{_}1365{_}But breakfast is ready, Miss.
10123{_}1366{_}I came to call you."
10123{_}1367{_}"Thank you," said Beth, turning to walk beside the housekeeper.
10123{_}1368{_}According to Aunt Jane's instructions the breakfast was served in her own room, and presently Louise, dressed in a light silk kimona, came in bearing her tray "to keep her cousin company," she laughingly announced.
10123{_}1369{_}"I should have slept an hour longer," she yawned, over her chocolate, "but old Misery--who seems rightly named--insisted on waking me, just that I might eat.
10123{_}1370{_}Isn't this a funny establishment?"
10123{_}1371{_}"It's different from everything I'm used to," answered Beth, gravely; "but it seems very pleasant here, and everyone is most kind and attentive."
10123{_}1372{_}"Now I'll dress," said Louise, "and we'll take a long walk together, and see the place."
10123{_}1373{_}So it happened that Kenneth clattered down the road on the sorrel mare just a moment before the girls emerged from the house, and while he was riding off his indignation at their presence at Elmhurst, they were doing just what his horrified imagination had depicted--that is, penetrating to all parts of the grounds, to every nook in the spacious old gardens and even to the stables, where Beth endeavored to make a friend of old Donald the coachman.
10123{_}1374{_}However, the gray-whiskered Scotsman was not to be taken by storm, even by a pretty face.
10123{_}1375{_}His loyalty to "the boy" induced him to be wary in associating with these strange "young females" and although he welcomed them to the stable with glum civility he withheld his opinion of them until he should know them better.
10123{_}1376{_}In their rambles the girls found Kenneth's own stair, and were sitting upon it when Phibbs came to summon Louise to attend upon Aunt Jane.
10123{_}1377{_}She obeyed with alacrity, for she wished to know more of the queer relative whose guest she had become.
10123{_}1378{_}"Sit down," said Aunt Jane, very graciously, as the girl entered.
10123{_}1379{_}Louise leaned over the chair, kissed her and patted her cheek affectionately, and then shook up the pillows to make them more comfortable.
10123{_}1380{_}"I want you to talk to me," announced Aunt Jane, "and to tell me something of the city and the society in which you live.
10123{_}1381{_}I've been so long dead to the world that I've lost track of people and things."
10123{_}1382{_}"Let me dress your hair at the same time," said Louise, pleadingly.
10123{_}1383{_}"It looks really frowsy, and I can talk while I work."
10123{_}1384{_}"I can't lift my left hand," said the invalid, flushing, "and Phibbs is a stupid ass."
10123{_}1385{_}"Never mind, I can make it look beautiful in half a jiffy," said the girl, standing behind the chair and drawing deftly the hairpins from Aunt Jane's scanty grey locks, "and you can't imagine how it pleases me to fuss over anyone."
10123{_}1386{_}It was surprising how meekly Aunt Jane submitted to this ordeal, but she plied the girl with many shrewd questions and Louise, busily working in a position where the old woman could not see her face, never hesitated for an answer.
10123{_}1387{_}She knew all the recent gossip of fashionable society, and retailed it glibly.
10123{_}1388{_}She had met this celebrity at a ball and that one at a reception, and she described them minutely, realizing that Aunt Jane would never be in a position to contradict any assertion she might choose to make.
10123{_}1389{_}Indeed, Aunt Jane was really startled.
10123{_}1390{_}"However did your mother manage to gain an entree into society?"
10123{_}1391{_}she asked.
10123{_}1392{_}"Your father was a poor man and of little account.
10123{_}1393{_}I know, for he was my own brother."
10123{_}1394{_}"He left us a very respectable life insurance," said Louise, demurely, "and my mother had many friends who were glad to introduce us to good society when we were able to afford such a luxury.
10123{_}1395{_}Father died twelve years ago, you know, and for several years, while I was at school, mother lived very quietly.
10123{_}1396{_}Then she decided it was time I made my debut, but for the last season we have been rather gay, I admit."
10123{_}1397{_}"Are you rich?"
10123{_}1398{_}asked Aunt Jane, sharply.
10123{_}1399{_}"Mercy, no!"
10123{_}1400{_}laughed Louise, who had finished her work and now sat her aunt's feet.
10123{_}1401{_}"But we have enough for our requirements, and that makes us feel quite independent.
10123{_}1402{_}By the way, auntie, I want to return that check you sent me.
10123{_}1403{_}It was awfully good and generous of you, but I didn't need it, you know, and so I want you to take it back."
10123{_}1404{_}She drew the slip of paper from her pocket and pressed it into Aunt Jane's hand.
10123{_}1405{_}"It's quite enough for you to give me this nice treat in the country," resumed the girl, calmly.
10123{_}1406{_}"The change from the city will do me a world of good, and as I wanted to be quiet, and rest I declined all my other invitations for the summer to accept yours.
10123{_}1407{_}Isn't it glorious that we can get acquainted at last?
10123{_}1408{_}And I quite love Elmhurst, already!"
10123{_}1409{_}Aunt Jane was equally surprised and gratified.
10123{_}1410{_}The return of the check for a hundred dollars was very pleasant.
10123{_}1411{_}She had drawn a similar check for each of her three nieces, believing that it would be necessary for her to meet their expenses, and she had considered the expenditure in the nature of a business transaction.
10123{_}1412{_}But Patricia had flung one check in her face, practically, and now Louise had voluntarily returned another, because she did not need the money.
10123{_}1413{_}Really, Jane Merrick was accomplishing her purpose for less money than she had expected, and she had hoarded her wealth for so many years that she disliked to spend any of it foolishly.
10123{_}1414{_}Louise had read her nature correctly.
10123{_}1415{_}It had been a little hard to return so large a check, but the girl's policy was not to appear before Aunt Jane as a poor relation, but rather as a young lady fitted by social education and position to become a gracious mistress of Elmhurst.
10123{_}1416{_}This she believed would give her a powerful advantage over all competitors.
10123{_}1417{_}Whether she was right or not in this surmise it is certain that she rose several points in Aunt Jane's estimation during this interview, and when she was dismissed it was so graciously that she told herself the money her little plot had cost had been well expended.
10123{_}1418{_}Afterward Elizabeth was summoned to attend her aunt.
10123{_}1419{_}"I want to be amused.
10123{_}1420{_}Can you read aloud?"
10123{_}1421{_}said the invalid.
10123{_}1422{_}"Not very well, I'm afraid.
10123{_}1423{_}But I'll be glad to try," answered Beth.
10123{_}1424{_}"What do you like?"
10123{_}1425{_}"Select your own book," said Aunt Jane, pointing to a heap of volumes beside her.
10123{_}1426{_}The girl hesitated.
10123{_}1427{_}Louise would doubtless have chosen a romance, or some light tale sure to interest for the hour, and so amuse the old lady.
10123{_}1428{_}But Beth erroneously judged that the aged and infirm love sober and scholarly books, and picked out a treatise that proved ineffably dull and tedious.
10123{_}1429{_}Aunt Jane sniffed, and then smiled slyly and proceeded to settle herself for a nap.
10123{_}1430{_}If the girl was a fool, let her be properly punished.
10123{_}1431{_}Beth read for an hour, uncertain whether her aunt were intensely interested or really asleep.
10123{_}1432{_}At the end of that dreadful period old Misery entered and aroused the sleeper without ceremony.
10123{_}1433{_}"What's the matter?"
10123{_}1434{_}asked Aunt Jane, querrulously, for she resented being disturbed.
10123{_}1435{_}"There's a man to see you, Miss."
10123{_}1436{_}"Send him about his business!"
10123{_}1437{_}"But--"  "I won't see him, I tell you!"
10123{_}1438{_}"But he says he's your brother, Miss."
10123{_}1439{_}"Who?"
10123{_}1440{_}"Your brother."
10123{_}1441{_}Miss Jane stared as if bewildered.
10123{_}1442{_}"Your brother John, Miss."
10123{_}1443{_}The invalid sank back upon her cushions with a sigh of resignation.
10123{_}1444{_}"I thought he was dead, long ago; but if he's alive I suppose I'll have to see him," she said.
10123{_}1445{_}"Elizabeth, leave the room.
10123{_}1446{_}Misery, send the man here!"
10123{_}1447{_}CHAPTER XII.
10123{_}1448{_}UNCLE JOHN GETS ACQUAINTED.
10123{_}1449{_}Beth went out to find Louise, and discovered her standing near the stables, where a boy was rubbing down the sides of a sorrel mare with wisps of straw.
10123{_}1450{_}"Something has happened," she said to Louise in a troubled voice.
10123{_}1451{_}"What?"
10123{_}1452{_}"A man has arrived who says he is Aunt Jane's brother."
10123{_}1453{_}"Impossible!
10123{_}1454{_}Have you seen him?"
10123{_}1455{_}"No; he says he's Aunt Jane's brother John."
10123{_}1456{_}"Oh; I know.
10123{_}1457{_}The peddler, or tinker, or something or other who disappeared years ago.
10123{_}1458{_}But it doesn't matter."
10123{_}1459{_}"It may matter a good deal," said practical Beth.
10123{_}1460{_}"Aunt Jane may leave him her money."
10123{_}1461{_}"Why, he's older than she is.
10123{_}1462{_}I've heard mother say he was the eldest of the family.
10123{_}1463{_}Aunt Jane wont leave her money to an old man, you may be sure."
10123{_}1464{_}Beth felt a little reassured at this, and stood for a moment beside Louise watching the boy.
10123{_}1465{_}Presently Oscar came to him, and after touching his hat respectfully took the mare and led her into the stable.
10123{_}1466{_}The boy turned away, with his hands in his pockets, and strolled up a path, unaware that the two dreaded girls had been observing him.
10123{_}1467{_}"I wonder who that is," said Beth.
10123{_}1468{_}"We'll find out," returned Louise.
10123{_}1469{_}"I took him for a stable boy, at first.
10123{_}1470{_}But Oscar seemed to treat him as a superior."
10123{_}1471{_}She walked into the stable, followed by her cousin, and found the groom tying the mare.
10123{_}1472{_}"Who was the young man?"
10123{_}1473{_}she asked.
10123{_}1474{_}"Which young man, Miss?"
10123{_}1475{_}"The one who has just arrived with the horse."
10123{_}1476{_}"Oh; that's Master Kenneth, Miss," answered Oscar, with a grin.
10123{_}1477{_}"Where did he come from?"
10123{_}1478{_}"Master Kenneth?
10123{_}1479{_}Why, he lives here."
10123{_}1480{_}"At the house?"
10123{_}1481{_}"Yes, Miss."
10123{_}1482{_}"Who is he?"
10123{_}1483{_}"Master Tom's nephew--he as used to own Elmhurst, you know."
10123{_}1484{_}"Mr. Thomas Bradley?"
10123{_}1485{_}"The same, Miss."
10123{_}1486{_}"Ah.
10123{_}1487{_}How long has Master Kenneth lived here?"
10123{_}1488{_}"A good many years.
10123{_}1489{_}I can't just remember how long."
10123{_}1490{_}"Thank you, Oscar."
10123{_}1491{_}The girls walked away, and when they were alone Louise remarked:  "Here is a more surprising discovery than Uncle John, Beth.
10123{_}1492{_}The boy has a better right than any of us to inherit Elmhurst."
10123{_}1493{_}"Then why did Aunt Jane send for us?"
10123{_}1494{_}"It's a mystery, dear.
10123{_}1495{_}Let us try to solve it."
10123{_}1496{_}"Come; we'll ask the housekeeper," said Beth.
10123{_}1497{_}"I'm sure old Misery will tell us all we want to know."
10123{_}1498{_}So they returned to the house and, with little difficulty, found the old housekeeper.
10123{_}1499{_}"Master Kenneth?"
10123{_}1500{_}she exclaimed.
10123{_}1501{_}"Why, he's just Master Tom's nephew, that's all."
10123{_}1502{_}"Is this his home?"
10123{_}1503{_}asked Beth.
10123{_}1504{_}"All the home he's got, my dear.
10123{_}1505{_}His father and mother are both dead, and Miss Jane took him to care for just because she thought Master Tom would 'a' liked it."
10123{_}1506{_}"Is she fond of him?"
10123{_}1507{_}enquired Louise.
10123{_}1508{_}"Fond of the boy?
10123{_}1509{_}Why, Miss Jane just hates him, for a fact.
10123{_}1510{_}She won't even see him, or have him near her.
10123{_}1511{_}So he keeps to his little room in the left wing, and eats and sleeps there."
10123{_}1512{_}"It's strange," remarked Beth, thoughtfully.
10123{_}1513{_}"Isn't he a nice boy?"
10123{_}1514{_}"We're all very fond of Master Kenneth," replied the housekeeper, simply.
10123{_}1515{_}"But I'll admit he's a queer lad, and has a bad temper.
10123{_}1516{_}It may be due to his lack of bringin' up, you know; for he just runs wild, and old Mr. Chase, who comes from the village to tutor him, is a poor lot, and lets the boy do as he pleases.
10123{_}1517{_}For that reason he won't study, and he won't work, and I'm sure I don't know whatever will become of him, when Miss Jane dies."
10123{_}1518{_}"Thank you," said Beth, much relieved, and the girls walked away with lighter hearts.
10123{_}1519{_}"There's no danger in that quarter, after all," said Louise, gaily.
10123{_}1520{_}"The boy is a mere hanger-on.
10123{_}1521{_}You see, Aunt Jane's old sweetheart, Thomas Bradley, left everything to her when he died, and she can do as she likes with it."
10123{_}1522{_}After luncheon, which they ate alone and unattended save by the maid Susan, who was old Misery's daughter, the girls walked away to the rose arbor, where Beth declared they could read or sew quite undisturbed.
10123{_}1523{_}But sitting upon the bench they found a little old man, his legs extended, his hands thrust deep into his pockets, and a look of calm meditation upon his round and placid face.
10123{_}1524{_}Between his teeth was a black brier pipe, which he puffed lazily.
10123{_}1525{_}Beth was for drawing back, but Louise took her arm and drew her forward.
10123{_}1526{_}"Isn't this Uncle John?"
10123{_}1527{_}she asked.
10123{_}1528{_}The little man turned his eyes upon them, withdrew his hands from his pockets and his pipe from his mouth, and then bowed profoundly.
10123{_}1529{_}"If you are my nieces, then I am Uncle John," he said, affably.
10123{_}1530{_}"Sit down, my dears, and let us get acquainted."
10123{_}1531{_}Louise smiled, and her rapid survey took in the man's crumpled and somewhat soiled shirt-front, the frayed black necktie that seemed to have done years of faithful service, and the thick and dusty cow-hide boots.
10123{_}1532{_}His clothing was old and much worn, and the thought crossed her mind that Oscar the groom was far neater in appearance than this newly-found relative.
10123{_}1533{_}Beth merely noticed that Uncle John was neither dignified nor imposing in appearance.
10123{_}1534{_}She sat down beside him--leaving a wide space between them--with a feeling of disappointment that he was "like all the rest of the Merricks."
10123{_}1535{_}"You have just arrived, we hear," remarked Louise.
10123{_}1536{_}"Yes.
10123{_}1537{_}Walked up from the station this forenoon," said Uncle John.
10123{_}1538{_}"Come to see Jane, you know, but hadn't any idea I'd find two nieces.
10123{_}1539{_}Hadn't any idea I possessed two nieces, to be honest about it."
10123{_}1540{_}"I believe you have three," said Louise, in an, amused tone.
10123{_}1541{_}"Three?
10123{_}1542{_}Who's the other?"
10123{_}1543{_}"Why, Patricia Doyle."
10123{_}1544{_}"Doyle?
10123{_}1545{_}Doyle?
10123{_}1546{_}Don't remember the name."
10123{_}1547{_}"I believe your sister Violet married a man named Doyle."
10123{_}1548{_}"So she did.
10123{_}1549{_}Captain Doyle--or Major Doyle--or some such fellow.
10123{_}1550{_}But what is your name?"
10123{_}1551{_}"I am Louise Merrick, your brother Will's daughter."
10123{_}1552{_}"Oh!
10123{_}1553{_}And you?"
10123{_}1554{_}turning to Beth.
10123{_}1555{_}"My mother was Julia Merrick," said Beth, not very graciously.
10123{_}1556{_}"She married Professor DeGraf.
10123{_}1557{_}I am Elizabeth DeGraf."
10123{_}1558{_}"Yes, yes," observed Uncle John, nodding his head.
10123{_}1559{_}"I remember Julia very well, as a girl.
10123{_}1560{_}She used to put on a lot of airs, and jaw father because he wouldn't have the old top-buggy painted every spring.
10123{_}1561{_}Same now as ever, I s'pose?"
10123{_}1562{_}Beth did not reply.
10123{_}1563{_}"And Will's dead, and out of his troubles, I hope," continued Uncle John, reflectively.
10123{_}1564{_}"He wrote me once that his wife had nearly driven him crazy.
10123{_}1565{_}Perhaps she murdered him in his sleep--eh, Louise?"
10123{_}1566{_}"Sir," said Louise, much offended, "you are speaking of my mother."
10123{_}1567{_}"Ah, yes.
10123{_}1568{_}It's the same one your father spoke of," he answered, unmoved.
10123{_}1569{_}"But that's neither here nor there.
10123{_}1570{_}The fact is, I've found two nieces," looking shrewdly from one face into the other, "and I seem to be in luck, for you're quite pretty and ladylike, my dears."
10123{_}1571{_}"Thank you," said Louise, rather coldly.
10123{_}1572{_}"You're a competent judge, sir, I suppose."
10123{_}1573{_}"Tolerable," he responded, with a chuckle.
10123{_}1574{_}"So good a judge that I've kep' single all my life."
10123{_}1575{_}"Where did you come from?"
10123{_}1576{_}asked the girl.
10123{_}1577{_}"From out on the coast," tossing his grizzled head toward the west.
10123{_}1578{_}"What brought you back here, after all these years?"
10123{_}1579{_}"Family affection, I guess.
10123{_}1580{_}Wanted to find out what folks yet belonged to me."
10123{_}1581{_}An awkward silence followed this, during which Uncle John relighted his pipe and Beth sat in moody silence.
10123{_}1582{_}Louise drew a pattern in the gravel with the end of her parasol.
10123{_}1583{_}This new uncle, she reflected, might become an intolerable bore, if she encouraged his frank familiarity.
10123{_}1584{_}"Now that you are here," she said, presently, "what are you going to do?"
10123{_}1585{_}"Nothing, my dear."
10123{_}1586{_}"Have you any money?"
10123{_}1587{_}He looked at her with a droll expression.
10123{_}1588{_}"Might have expected that question, my dear," said he; "but it's rather hard to answer.
10123{_}1589{_}If I say no, you'll be afraid I'll want to borrow a little spendin' money, now an' then; and if I say yes, you'll take me for a Rockyfeller."
10123{_}1590{_}"Not exactly," smiled Louise.
10123{_}1591{_}"Well, then, if I figure close I won't have to borrow," he responded, gravely.
10123{_}1592{_}"And here's Jane, my sister, just rolling in wealth that she don't know what to do with.
10123{_}1593{_}And she's invited me to stay a while.
10123{_}1594{_}So let's call the money question settled, my dear."
10123{_}1595{_}Another silence ensued.
10123{_}1596{_}Louise had satisfied her curiosity concerning her new uncle, and Beth had never had any.
10123{_}1597{_}There was nothing more to say, and as Uncle John showed no intention of abandoning the arbored seat, it was evident they must go themselves.
10123{_}1598{_}Louise was about to rise when the man remarked:  "Jane won't last long".
10123{_}1599{_}"You think not?"
10123{_}1600{_}she asked.
10123{_}1601{_}"She says she's half dead a'ready, and I believe it.
10123{_}1602{_}It's about time, you know.
10123{_}1603{_}She's let her temper and restless disposition wear her out.
10123{_}1604{_}Pretty soon she'll blow out, like a candle.
10123{_}1605{_}All that worries her is to keep alive until she can decide who to leave her money to.
10123{_}1606{_}That's why you're here, I s'pose, my dears.
10123{_}1607{_}How do you like being on exhibition, an' goin' through your paces, like a bunch o' trotting hosses, to see which is worth the most?"
10123{_}1608{_}"Uncle John," said Beth, "I had hoped I would like you.
10123{_}1609{_}But if you are going to be so very disagreeable, I'll have nothing more to do with you!"
10123{_}1610{_}With this she arose and marched up the path, vastly indignant, and Louise marched beside her.
10123{_}1611{_}At the bend in the walk they glanced back, and saw Uncle John sitting upon the bench all doubled up and shaking with silent laughter.
10123{_}1612{_}"He's a queer old man," said Beth, flushing; "but he's impudent and half a fool."
10123{_}1613{_}"Don't judge hastily, Beth," replied Louise, reflectively.
10123{_}1614{_}"I can't make up my mind, just yet, whether Uncle John is a fool or not."
10123{_}1615{_}"Anyhow," snapped Beth, "he's laughing at us."
10123{_}1616{_}"And that," said her cousin, softly, "is the strongest evidence of his sanity.
10123{_}1617{_}Beth, my love, Aunt Jane has placed us in a most ridiculous position."
10123{_}1618{_}That evening at dinner they met Uncle John again, seated opposite Aunt Jane in the great dining hall.
10123{_}1619{_}The mistress of Elmhurst always dressed for this meal and tonight she wore a rich black silk and had her invalid chair wheeled to her place at the head of the table.
10123{_}1620{_}Uncle John had simply changed his old black necktie for a soiled white one.
10123{_}1621{_}Otherwise his apparel was the same as before, and his stubby gray hair was in a sad state of disarray.
10123{_}1622{_}But his round face wore a cheerful smile, nevertheless, and Aunt Jane seemed not to observe anything _outre_ in her brother's appearance.
10123{_}1623{_}And so the meal passed pleasantly enough.
10123{_}1624{_}After it was finished Uncle John strolled into the garden to smoke his pipe under the stars and Louise sang a few songs for Aunt Jane in the dimly-lit drawing room.
10123{_}1625{_}Beth, who was a music teacher's daughter, could not sing at all.
10123{_}1626{_}It was some time later when John Merrick came to his sister's room to bid her good night.
10123{_}1627{_}"Well," she asked him, "what do you think of the girls?"
10123{_}1628{_}"My nieces?"
10123{_}1629{_}"Yes."
10123{_}1630{_}"During my lifetime," said the old man, "I've always noticed that girls are just girls--and nothing more.
10123{_}1631{_}Jane, your sex is a puzzle that ain't worth the trouble solving.
10123{_}1632{_}You're all alike, and what little I've seen of my nieces convinces me they're regulation females--no better nor worse than their kind."
10123{_}1633{_}"Louise seems a capable girl," declared Aunt Jane, musingly.
10123{_}1634{_}"I didn't care much for her, at first; but she improves on acquaintance.
10123{_}1635{_}She has been well trained by her mother, and is very ladylike and agreeable."
10123{_}1636{_}"She's smarter than the other one, but not so honest," said Uncle John.
10123{_}1637{_}"Beth has no tact at all," replied Aunt Jane.
10123{_}1638{_}"But then, she's younger than Louise."
10123{_}1639{_}"If you're trying to figure out what they are, and what they are not," returned the man, "you've got a hard job on your hands, Jane, and like as not you'll make a mistake in the end.
10123{_}1640{_}Where's the other niece?
10123{_}1641{_}Aren't there three of them?"
10123{_}1642{_}"Yes.
10123{_}1643{_}The other's coming.
10123{_}1644{_}Silas Watson, my lawyer, has just telegraphed from New York that he's bringing Patricia back with him."
10123{_}1645{_}"Had to send for her, eh?"
10123{_}1646{_}"Yes.
10123{_}1647{_}She's Irish, and if I remember rightly her father is a disgraceful old reprobate, who caused poor Violet no end of worry.
10123{_}1648{_}The girl may be like him, for she wrote me a dreadful letter, scolding me because I hadn't kept her parents supplied with money, and refusing to become my guest."
10123{_}1649{_}"But she's changed her mind?"
10123{_}1650{_}"I sent Watson after her, and he's bringing her.
10123{_}1651{_}I wanted to see what the girl is like."
10123{_}1652{_}Uncle John whistled a few bars of an ancient tune.
10123{_}1653{_}"My advice is," he said, finally, "to let 'em draw cuts for Elmhurst.
10123{_}1654{_}If you want to leave your money to the best o' the lot, you're as sure of striking it right that way as any other."
10123{_}1655{_}"Nonsense!"
10123{_}1656{_}said Jane Merrick, sharply.
10123{_}1657{_}"I don't want to leave my money to the best of the lot."
10123{_}1658{_}"No?"
10123{_}1659{_}"By no means.
10123{_}1660{_}I want to leave it to the one I prefer--whether she's the best or not."
10123{_}1661{_}"I see.
10123{_}1662{_}Jane, I'll repeat my former observation.
10123{_}1663{_}Your sex is a puzzle that isn't worth solving.
10123{_}1664{_}Good night, old girl."
10123{_}1665{_}"Good night, John."
10123{_}1666{_}CHAPTER XIII.
10123{_}1667{_}THE OTHER NIECE.
10123{_}1668{_}Patricia sat down opposite her Aunt Jane.
10123{_}1669{_}She still wore her hat and the gray wrap.
10123{_}1670{_}"Well, here I am," she exclaimed, with a laugh; "but whether I ought to be here or not I have my doubts."
10123{_}1671{_}Aunt Jane surveyed her critically.
10123{_}1672{_}"You're a queer little thing," she said, bluntly.
10123{_}1673{_}"I wonder why I took so much trouble to get you."
10123{_}1674{_}"So do I," returned Patsy, her eyes twinkling.
10123{_}1675{_}"You'll probably be sorry for it."
10123{_}1676{_}Lawyer Watson, who had remained standing, now broke in nervously.
10123{_}1677{_}"I explained to Miss Doyle," said he, "that you were ill, and wanted to see her.
10123{_}1678{_}And she kindly consented to come to Elmhurst for a few days."
10123{_}1679{_}"You see," said Patsy, "I'd just got Daddy away on his vacation, to visit his old colonel.
10123{_}1680{_}I've wanted him to go this three years back, but he couldn't afford it until I got a raise this Spring.
10123{_}1681{_}He'll have a glorious old time with the colonel, and they'll fish and hunt and drink whiskey all day, and fight the war all over again every evening.
10123{_}1682{_}So I was quite by myself when Mr. Watson came to me and wouldn't take no for his answer."
10123{_}1683{_}"Why did you object to come here?"
10123{_}1684{_}asked Aunt Jane.
10123{_}1685{_}"Well, I didn't know you; and I didn't especially want to know you.
10123{_}1686{_}Not that I bear grudges, understand, although you've been little of a friend to my folks these past years.
10123{_}1687{_}But you are rich and proud--and I suspect you're a little cross, Aunt Jane--while we are poor and proud and like to live our lives in our own way."
10123{_}1688{_}"Are you a working girl?"
10123{_}1689{_}enquired Miss Merrick.
10123{_}1690{_}"Surely," said Patsy, "and drawing a big lump of salary every Saturday night.
10123{_}1691{_}I'm a hair-dresser, you know--and by the way, Aunt Jane, it puzzles me to find a certain kink in your hair that I thought I'd invented myself."
10123{_}1692{_}"Louise dressed my hair this way," said Miss Merrick, a bit stiffly.
10123{_}1693{_}"Your maid?"
10123{_}1694{_}"My niece, Louise Merrick."
10123{_}1695{_}Patsy whistled, and then clapped her hand over her mouth and looked grave.
10123{_}1696{_}"Is she here?"
10123{_}1697{_}she asked, a moment later.
10123{_}1698{_}"Yes, and your other cousin, Elizabeth De Graf, is here also."
10123{_}1699{_}"That's just the trouble," cried Patsy, energetically.
10123{_}1700{_}"That's why I didn't want to come, you know."
10123{_}1701{_}"I don't understand you, Patricia."
10123{_}1702{_}"Why, it's as plain as the nose on your face, even if I hadn't pumped Mr. Watson until I got the truth out of him.
10123{_}1703{_}You want us girls here just to compare us with each other, and pick out the one you like best."
10123{_}1704{_}"Well?"
10123{_}1705{_}"The others you'll throw over, and the favorite will get your money."
10123{_}1706{_}"Haven't I a right to do that?"
10123{_}1707{_}asked the invalid, in an amazed tone.
10123{_}1708{_}"Perhaps you have.
10123{_}1709{_}But we may as well understand each other right now, Aunt Jane.
10123{_}1710{_}I won't touch a penny of your money, under any circumstances."
10123{_}1711{_}"I don't think you will, Patricia."
10123{_}1712{_}The girl laughed, with a joyous, infectious merriment that was hard to resist.
10123{_}1713{_}"Stick to that, aunt, and there's no reason we shouldn't be friends," she said, pleasantly.
10123{_}1714{_}"I don't mind coming to see you, for it will give me a bit of a rest and the country is beautiful just now.
10123{_}1715{_}More than that, I believe I shall like you.
10123{_}1716{_}You've had your own way a long time, and you've grown crochetty and harsh and disagreeable; but there are good lines around your mouth and eyes, and your nature's liable to soften and get sunny again.
10123{_}1717{_}I'm sure I hope so.
10123{_}1718{_}So, if you'd like me to stay a few days, I'll take off my things and make myself at home.
10123{_}1719{_}But I'm out of the race for your money, and I'll pay my way from now on just as I have always done."
10123{_}1720{_}Silas Watson watched Aunt Jane's face during this speech with an anxious and half-frightened expression upon his own.
10123{_}1721{_}No one but himself had ever dared to talk to Jane Merrick as plainly as this before, and he wondered how she would accept such frankness from a young girl.
10123{_}1722{_}But Patricia's manner was not at all offensive.
10123{_}1723{_}Her big eyes were as frank as her words, but they glistened with kindliness and good nature, and it was evident the girl had no doubt at all of her aunt's reply, for she straightway begun to take off her hat.
10123{_}1724{_}The invalid had kept her eyes sternly fastened upon her young niece ever since the beginning of the interview.
10123{_}1725{_}Now she reached out a hand and touched her bell.
10123{_}1726{_}"Misery," she said to the old housekeeper, "show my niece, Miss Patricia, to the rose chamber.
10123{_}1727{_}And see that she is made comfortable."
10123{_}1728{_}"Thank you," said Patsy, jumping up to go.
10123{_}1729{_}"Make yourself perfectly free of the place," continued Aunt Jane, in an even tone, turning to Patricia, "and have as good a time as you can.
10123{_}1730{_}I'm afraid it's rather stupid here for girls, but that can't be helped.
10123{_}1731{_}Stay as long as you please, and go home whenever you like; but while you are here, if you ever feel like chatting with a harsh and disagreeable old woman, come to me at any time and you will be welcome."
10123{_}1732{_}Patsy, standing before her, looked down into her worn face with a pitying expression.
10123{_}1733{_}"Ah!
10123{_}1734{_}I've been cruel to you," she exclaimed, impulsively, "and I didn't mean to hurt you at all, Aunt Jane.
10123{_}1735{_}You must forgive me.
10123{_}1736{_}It's just my blunt Irish way, you see; but if I hadn't been drawn to you from the first I wouldn't have said a word--good or bad!"
10123{_}1737{_}"Go now," replied Aunt Jane, turning in her chair rather wearily.
10123{_}1738{_}"But come to me again whenever you like."
10123{_}1739{_}Patsy nodded, and followed the housekeeper to the rose chamber--the prettiest room old Elmhurst possessed, with broad windows opening directly upon the finest part of the garden.
10123{_}1740{_}Lawyer Watson sat opposite his old friend for some moments in thoughtful silence.
10123{_}1741{_}"The child is impossible."
10123{_}1742{_}he said, at last.
10123{_}1743{_}"You think so?"
10123{_}1744{_}she enquired, moodily.
10123{_}1745{_}"Absolutely.
10123{_}1746{_}Either of the others would make a better Lady of Elmhurst.
10123{_}1747{_}Yet I like the little thing, I confess.
10123{_}1748{_}She quite won my old heart after I had known her for five minutes.
10123{_}1749{_}But money would ruin her.
10123{_}1750{_}She's a child of the people, and ought not to be raised from her proper level.
10123{_}1751{_}Jane, Jane--you're making a grave mistake in all this.
10123{_}1752{_}Why don't you do the only right thing in your power, and leave Elmhurst to Kenneth?"
10123{_}1753{_}"You bore me, Silas," she answered, coldly.
10123{_}1754{_}"The boy is the most impossible of all."
10123{_}1755{_}It was the old protest and the old reply.
10123{_}1756{_}He had hardly expected anything different.
10123{_}1757{_}After a period of thought he asked;  "What is this I hear about John Merrick having returned from the West?"
10123{_}1758{_}"He came yesterday.
10123{_}1759{_}It was a great surprise to me."
10123{_}1760{_}"I never knew this brother, I believe."
10123{_}1761{_}"No; he had gone away before I became acquainted with either you or Tom."
10123{_}1762{_}"What sort of a man is he?"
10123{_}1763{_}"Honest and simple, hard-headed and experienced."
10123{_}1764{_}"Is he independent?"
10123{_}1765{_}"I believe so; he has never mentioned his affairs to me.
10123{_}1766{_}But he has worked hard all his life, he says, and now means to end his days peacefully.
10123{_}1767{_}John is not especially refined in his manner, nor did he have much of an education; but he seems to be a good deal of a man, for all that.
10123{_}1768{_}I am very glad he appeared at Elmhurst just at this time."
10123{_}1769{_}"You had believed him dead?"
10123{_}1770{_}"Yes.
10123{_}1771{_}He had passed out of my life completely, and I never knew what became of him."
10123{_}1772{_}"He must be an eccentric person," said Mr. Watson, with a smile.
10123{_}1773{_}"He is."
10123{_}1774{_}she acknowledged.
10123{_}1775{_}"But blood is thicker than water, Silas, and I'm glad brother John is here at last."
10123{_}1776{_}A little later the lawyer left her and picked his way through the gardens until he came to Kenneth's wing and the stair that led to his room.
10123{_}1777{_}Here he paused a moment, finding himself surrounded by a profound stillness, broken only by the chirping of the birds in the shrubbery.
10123{_}1778{_}Perhaps Kenneth was not in.
10123{_}1779{_}He half decided to retrace his steps, but finally mounted the stair softly and stood within the doorway of the room.
10123{_}1780{_}The boy and a little stout man were playing chess at a table, and both were in a deep study of the game.
10123{_}1781{_}The boy's back was toward him, but the man observed the newcomer and gave a nod.
10123{_}1782{_}Then he dropped his eyes again to the table.
10123{_}1783{_}Kenneth was frowning sullenly.
10123{_}1784{_}"You're bound to lose the pawn, whichever way you play," said the little man quietly.
10123{_}1785{_}The boy gave an angry cry, and thrust the table from him, sending the chess-men clattering into a corner.
10123{_}1786{_}Instantly the little man leaned over and grasped the boy by the collar, and with a sudden jerk landed him across his own fat knees.
10123{_}1787{_}Then, while the prisoner screamed and struggled, the man brought his hand down with a slap that echoed throughout the room, and continued the operation until Master Kenneth had received a sound spanking.
10123{_}1788{_}Then he let the boy slip to the floor, from whence he arose slowly and backed toward the door, scowling and muttering angrily.
10123{_}1789{_}"You broke the bargain, and I kept my word," said Uncle John, calmly taking his pipe from his pocket and filling it.
10123{_}1790{_}"The compact was that if you raised a rough-house, like you did yesterday, and got unruly, that I'd give you a good thrashing.
10123{_}1791{_}Now, wasn't it?"
10123{_}1792{_}"Yes," acknowledged the boy.
10123{_}1793{_}"Well, that blamed temper o' your'n got away with you again, and you're well spanked for not heading it off.
10123{_}1794{_}Pick up the board.
10123{_}1795{_}Ken, my lad, and let's try it again."
10123{_}1796{_}The boy hesitated.
10123{_}1797{_}Then he looked around and saw Lawyer Watson, who had stood motionless by the doorway, and with a cry that was half a sob Kenneth threw himself into his old friend's arms and burst into a flood of tears.
10123{_}1798{_}Uncle John struck a match, and lighted his pipe.
10123{_}1799{_}"A bargain's a bargain," he observed, composedly.
10123{_}1800{_}"He whipped me!"
10123{_}1801{_}sobbed the boy.
10123{_}1802{_}"He whipped me like a child."
10123{_}1803{_}"Your own fault," said Uncle John.
10123{_}1804{_}"You wanted me to play a game with you, and I agreed, providin' you behaved yourself.
10123{_}1805{_}And you didn't.
10123{_}1806{_}Now, look here.
10123{_}1807{_}Do you blame me any?"
10123{_}1808{_}"No," said the boy.
10123{_}1809{_}"No harm's done, is there?"
10123{_}1810{_}"No."
10123{_}1811{_}"Then stop blubberin', and introduce me to your friend," continued Uncle John.
10123{_}1812{_}"Name's Watson, ain't it."
10123{_}1813{_}"Silas Watson, sir, at your service," said the lawyer, smiling.
10123{_}1814{_}"And this must be John Merrick, who I understand has arrived at Elmhurst during my absence."
10123{_}1815{_}"Exactly," said Uncle John, and the two men shook hands cordially.
10123{_}1816{_}"Glad to welcome you to Elmhurst, sir," continued the lawyer.
10123{_}1817{_}"I've known it ever since I was a boy, when it belonged to my dear friend Thomas Bradley.
10123{_}1818{_}And I hope you'll love it as much as I do, when you know it better."
10123{_}1819{_}"Bradley must have been a fool to give this place to Jane," said Uncle John, reflectively.
10123{_}1820{_}"He was in love, sir," observed the other, and they both smiled.
10123{_}1821{_}Then the lawyer turned to Kenneth.
10123{_}1822{_}"How are things going?"
10123{_}1823{_}he asked.
10123{_}1824{_}"Have the girls bothered you much, as yet?"
10123{_}1825{_}"No," said the boy.
10123{_}1826{_}"I keep out of their way."
10123{_}1827{_}"That's a good idea.
10123{_}1828{_}By the bye, sir," turning to John Merrick.
10123{_}1829{_}"I've just brought you a new niece."
10123{_}1830{_}"Patricia?"
10123{_}1831{_}"She prefers to be called Patsy.
10123{_}1832{_}A queer little thing; half Irish, you know."
10123{_}1833{_}"And half Merrick.
10123{_}1834{_}That's an odd combination, but the Irish may be able to stand it," said Uncle John.
10123{_}1835{_}"These nieces are more than I bargained for.
10123{_}1836{_}I came to see one relative, and find three more--and all women!"
10123{_}1837{_}"I think you'll like Patsy, anyhow.
10123{_}1838{_}And so will you, Kenneth."
10123{_}1839{_}The boy gave an indignant roar.
10123{_}1840{_}"I hate all girls!"
10123{_}1841{_}he said.
10123{_}1842{_}"You won't hate this one.
10123{_}1843{_}She's as wild and impulsive as you are, but better natured.
10123{_}1844{_}She'll make a good comrade, although she may box your ears once in a while."
10123{_}1845{_}The boy turned away sulkily, and began picking up the scattered chess-men.
10123{_}1846{_}The two men walked down the stair and strolled together through the garden.
10123{_}1847{_}"A strange boy," said Uncle John, presently.
10123{_}1848{_}"I'm glad to see you've made friends with him," replied the lawyer, earnestly.
10123{_}1849{_}"Until now he has had no one to befriend him but me, and at times he's so unmanageable that it worries me dreadfully."
10123{_}1850{_}"There's considerable character about the lad," said John Merrick; "but he's been spoiled and allowed to grow up wild, like a weed.
10123{_}1851{_}He's got it in him to make a criminal or a gentleman, whichever way his nature happens to develop."
10123{_}1852{_}"He ought to go to a military school," replied Lawyer Watson.
10123{_}1853{_}"Proper training would make a man of Kenneth; but I can't induce Jane to spend the money on him.
10123{_}1854{_}She gives him food and clothing and lodging--all of the simplest description--but there her generosity ends.
10123{_}1855{_}With thousands of dollars lying idle, she won't assist the only nephew of Tom Bradley to secure a proper education."
10123{_}1856{_}"Jane's queer, too," said that lady's brother, with a sigh.
10123{_}1857{_}"In fact, Mr. Watson, it's a queer world, and the longer I live in it the queerer I find it.
10123{_}1858{_}Once I thought it would be a good idea to regulate things myself and run the world as it ought to be run; but I gave it up long ago.
10123{_}1859{_}The world's a stage, they say; but the show ain't always amusing, by a long chalk, and sometimes I wish I didn't have a reserved seat."
10123{_}1860{_}CHAPTER XIV.
10123{_}1861{_}KENNETH IS FRIGHTENED.
10123{_}1862{_}Lawyer Watson, unable to direct events at Elmhurst, became a silent spectator of the little comedy being enacted there, and never regretted that, as Uncle John expressed it, he "had a reserved seat at the show."
10123{_}1863{_}Jane Merrick, formerly the most imperious and irrascible of women, had become wonderfully reserved since the arrival of her nieces, and was evidently making a sincere effort to study their diverse characters.
10123{_}1864{_}Day by day the invalid's health was failing visibly.
10123{_}1865{_}She had no more strokes of paralysis, but her left limb did not recover, and the numbness was gradually creeping upward toward her heart.
10123{_}1866{_}Perhaps the old woman appreciated this more fully than anyone else.
10123{_}1867{_}At any event, she became more gentle toward Phibbs and Misery, who mostly attended her, and showed as much consideration as possible for her nieces and her brother.
10123{_}1868{_}Silas Watson she kept constantly by her side.
10123{_}1869{_}He was her oldest and most trusted friend, and the only differences they had ever had were over the boy Kenneth, whom she stubbornly refused to favor.
10123{_}1870{_}Uncle John speedily became an established fixture at the place.
10123{_}1871{_}The servants grew accustomed to seeing him wander aimlessly about the grounds, his pipe always in his mouth, his hands usually in his pockets.
10123{_}1872{_}He had a pleasant word always for Donald or Oscar or James, but was not prone to long conversations.
10123{_}1873{_}Every evening, when he appeared at dinner, he wore his soiled white tie; at other times the black one was always in evidence; but other than this his dress underwent no change.
10123{_}1874{_}Even Kenneth came to wonder what the bundle had contained that Uncle John brought under his arm to Elmhurst.
10123{_}1875{_}The little man seemed from the first much attracted by his three nieces.
10123{_}1876{_}Notwithstanding Louise's constant snubs and Beth's haughty silence he was sure to meet them when they strolled out and try to engage them in conversation.
10123{_}1877{_}It was hard to resist his simple good nature, and the girls came in time to accept him as an inevitable companion, and Louise mischievously poked fun at him while Beth conscientiously corrected him in his speech and endeavored to improve his manners.
10123{_}1878{_}All this seemed very gratifying to Uncle John.
10123{_}1879{_}He thanked Beth very humbly for her kind attention, and laughed with Louise when she ridiculed his pudgy, round form and wondered if his bristly gray hair wouldn't make a good scrubbing brush.
10123{_}1880{_}Patsy didn't get along very well with her cousins.
10123{_}1881{_}From the first, when Louise recognized her, with well assumed surprise, as "the girl who had been sent to dress her hair," Patricia declared that their stations in life were entirely different.
10123{_}1882{_}"There's no use of our getting mixed up, just because we're cousins and all visiting Aunt Jane," she said.
10123{_}1883{_}"One of you will get her money, for I've told her I wouldn't touch a penny of it, and she has told me I wouldn't get the chance.
10123{_}1884{_}So one of you will be a great lady, while I shall always earn my own living.
10123{_}1885{_}I'll not stay long, anyhow; so just forget I'm here, and I'll amuse myself and try not to bother you."
10123{_}1886{_}Both Beth and Louise considered this very sensible, and took Patricia at her word.
10123{_}1887{_}Moreover, Phibbs had related to Beth, whose devoted adherent she was, all of the conversation between Aunt Jane and Patricia, from which the girls learned they had nothing to fear from their cousin's interference.
10123{_}1888{_}So they let her go her way, and the three only met at the state dinners, which Aunt Jane still attended, in spite of her growing weakness.
