10123{_}1889{_}Old Silas Watson, interested as he was in the result, found it hard to decide, after ten days, which of her nieces Jane Merrick most favored.
10123{_}1890{_}Personally he preferred that Beth should inherit, and frankly told his old friend that the girl would make the best mistress of Elmhurst.
10123{_}1891{_}Moreover, all the servants sang Beth's praises, from Misery and Phibbs down to Oscar and Susan.
10123{_}1892{_}Of course James the gardener favored no one, as the numerous strangers at Elmhurst kept him in a constant state of irritation, and his malady seemed even worse than usual.
10123{_}1893{_}He avoided everyone but his mistress, and although his work was now often neglected Miss Merrick made no complaint.
10123{_}1894{_}James' peculiarities were well understood and aroused nothing but sympathy.
10123{_}1895{_}Louise, however, had played her cards so well that all Beth's friends were powerless to eject the elder girl from Aunt Jane's esteem.
10123{_}1896{_}Louise had not only returned the check to her aunt, but she came often to sit beside her and cheer her with a budget of new social gossip, and no one could arrange the pillows so comfortably or stroke the tired head so gently as Louise.
10123{_}1897{_}And then, she was observing, and called Aunt Jane's attention to several ways of curtailing the household expenditures, which the woman's illness had forced her to neglect.
10123{_}1898{_}So Miss Merrick asked Louise to look over the weekly accounts, and in this way came to depend upon her almost as much as she did upon Lawyer Watson.
10123{_}1899{_}As for Patsy, she made no attempt whatever to conciliate her aunt, who seldom mentioned her name to the others but always brightened visibly when the girl came into her presence with her cheery speeches and merry laughter.
10123{_}1900{_}She never stayed long, but came and went, like a streak of sunshine, whenever the fancy seized her; and Silas Watson, shrewdly looking on, saw a new light in Jane's eyes as she looked after her wayward, irresponsible niece, and wondered if the bargain between them, regarding the money, would really hold good.
10123{_}1901{_}It was all an incomprehensible problem, this matter of the inheritance, and although the lawyer expected daily to be asked to draw up Jane Merrick's will, and had, indeed, prepared several forms, to be used in case of emergency, no word had yet passed her lips regarding her intentions.
10123{_}1902{_}Kenneth's life, during this period, was one of genuine misery.
10123{_}1903{_}It seemed to his morbid fancy that whatever path he might take, he was sure of running upon one or more of those detestable girls who were visiting at Elmhurst.
10123{_}1904{_}Even in Donald's harness-room he was not secure from interruption, for little Patsy was frequently perched upon the bench there, watching with serious eyes old Donald's motions, and laughing joyously when in his embarrassment he overturned a can of oil or buckled the wrong straps together.
10123{_}1905{_}Worse than all, this trying creature would saddle Nora, the sorrel mare, and dash away through the lanes like a tom-boy, leaving him only old Sam to ride--for Donald would allow no one to use the coach horses.
10123{_}1906{_}Sam was tall and boney, and had an unpleasant gait, so that the boy felt he was thoroughly justified in hating the girl who so frequently interfered with his whims.
10123{_}1907{_}Louise was at first quite interested in Kenneth, and resolved to force him to talk and become more sociable.
10123{_}1908{_}She caught him in a little summer-house one morning, from whence, there being but one entrance, he could not escape, and at once entered into conversation.
10123{_}1909{_}"Ah, you are Kenneth Forbes, I suppose," she began, pleasantly.
10123{_}1910{_}"I am very glad to make your acquaintance.
10123{_}1911{_}I am Louise Merrick, Miss Merrick's niece, and have come to visit her."
10123{_}1912{_}The boy shrank back as fur as possible, staring her full in the face, but made no reply.
10123{_}1913{_}"You needn't be afraid of me," continued Louise.
10123{_}1914{_}"I'm very fond of boys, and you must be nearly my own age."
10123{_}1915{_}Still no reply.
10123{_}1916{_}"I suppose you don't know much of girls and are rather shy," she persisted.
10123{_}1917{_}"But I want to be friendly and I hope you'll let me.
10123{_}1918{_}There's so much about this interesting old place that you can tell me, having lived here so many years.
10123{_}1919{_}Come, I'll sit beside you on this bench, and we'll have a good talk together."
10123{_}1920{_}"Go away!"
10123{_}1921{_}cried the boy, hoarsely, raising his hands as if to ward off her approach.
10123{_}1922{_}Louise looked surprised and pained.
10123{_}1923{_}"Why, we are almost cousins," she said.
10123{_}1924{_}"Cannot we become friends and comrades?"
10123{_}1925{_}With a sudden bound he dashed her aside, so rudely that she almost fell, and an instant later he had left the summer house and disappear among the hedges.
10123{_}1926{_}Louise laughed at her own discomfiture and gave up the attempt to make the boy's acquaintance.
10123{_}1927{_}"He's a regular savage," she told Beth, afterward, "and a little crazy, too, I suspect."
10123{_}1928{_}"Never mind," said Beth, philosophically.
10123{_}1929{_}"He's only a boy, and doesn't amount to anything, anyway.
10123{_}1930{_}After Aunt Jane dies he will probably go somewhere else to live.
10123{_}1931{_}Don't let us bother about him."
10123{_}1932{_}Kenneth's one persistent friend was Uncle John.
10123{_}1933{_}He came every day to the boy's room to play chess with him, and after that one day's punishment, which, singularly enough, Kenneth in no way resented, they got along very nicely together.
10123{_}1934{_}Uncle John was a shrewd player of the difficult game, but the boy was quick as a flash to see an advantage and use it against his opponent; so neither was ever sure of winning and the interest in the game was constantly maintained.
10123{_}1935{_}At evening also the little man often came to sit on the stair outside the boy's room and smoke his pipe, and frequently they would sit beneath the stars, absorbed in thought and without exchanging a single word.
10123{_}1936{_}Unfortunately, Louise and Beth soon discovered the boy's secluded retreat, and loved to torment him by entering his own bit of garden and even ascending the stairs to his little room.
10123{_}1937{_}He could easily escape them by running through the numerous upper halls of the mansion; but here he was liable to meet others, and his especial dread was encountering old Miss Merrick.
10123{_}1938{_}So he conceived a plan for avoiding the girls in another way.
10123{_}1939{_}In the hallway of the left wing, near his door, was a small ladder leading to the second story roof, and a dozen feet from the edge of the roof stood an old oak tree, on the further side of a tall hedge.
10123{_}1940{_}Kenneth managed to carry a plank to the roof, where, after several attempts, he succeeded in dropping one end into a crotch of the oak, thus connecting the edge of the roof with the tree by means of the narrow plank.
10123{_}1941{_}After this, at first sight of the girls in his end of the garden, he fled to the roof, ran across the improvised bridge, "shinned" down the tree and, hidden by the hedge, made good his escape.
10123{_}1942{_}The girls discovered this plan, and were wicked enough to surprise the boy often and force him to cross the dizzy plank to the tree.
10123{_}1943{_}Having frightened him away they would laugh and stroll on, highly amused at the evident fear they aroused in the only boy about the place.
10123{_}1944{_}Patricia, who was not in the other girls' secret, knew nothing of this little comedy and really disturbed Kenneth least of the three.
10123{_}1945{_}But he seemed to avoid her as much as he did the others.
10123{_}1946{_}She sooned learned from Oscar that the boy loved to ride as well as she did, and once or twice she met him on a lonely road perched on top of big Sam.
10123{_}1947{_}This led her to suspect she had thoughtlessly deprived him of his regular mount.
10123{_}1948{_}So one morning she said to the groom:  "Doesn't Kenneth usually ride Nora?"
10123{_}1949{_}"Yes, Miss," answered the man.
10123{_}1950{_}"Then I'd better take Sam this morning," she decided.
10123{_}1951{_}But the groom demurred.
10123{_}1952{_}"You won't like Sam, Miss," he said, "and he gets ugly at times and acts bad.
10123{_}1953{_}Master Kenneth won't use Nora today, I'm sure."
10123{_}1954{_}She hesitated.
10123{_}1955{_}"I think I'll ask him," said she, after a moment, and turned away into the garden, anxious to have this plausible opportunity to speak to the lonely boy.
10123{_}1956{_}CHAPTER XV.
10123{_}1957{_}PATSY MEETS WITH AN ACCIDENT.
10123{_}1958{_}"Get out of here!"
10123{_}1959{_}shouted the boy, angrily, as Patsy appeared at the foot of his stair.
10123{_}1960{_}"I won't!"
10123{_}1961{_}she answered indignantly.
10123{_}1962{_}"I've come to speak to you about the mare, and you'll just treat me decently or I'll know the reason why!"
10123{_}1963{_}But he didn't wait to hear this explanation.
10123{_}1964{_}He saw her advancing up the stairs, and fled in his usual hasty manner to the hall and up the ladder to the roof.
10123{_}1965{_}Patsy stepped back into the garden, vexed at his flight, and the next instant she saw him appear, upon the sloping roof and start to run down the plank.
10123{_}1966{_}Even as she looked the boy slipped, fell headlong, and slid swiftly downward.
10123{_}1967{_}In a moment he was over the edge, clutching wildly at the plank, which was a foot or more beyond his reach.
10123{_}1968{_}Headforemost he dove into space, but the clutching hand found something at last--the projecting hook of an old eaves-trough that had long since been removed--and to this he clung fast in spite of the jerk of his arrested body, which threatened to tear away his grip.
10123{_}1969{_}But his plight was desperate, nevertheless.
10123{_}1970{_}He was dangling in space, the hard pavement thirty feet below him, with no possible way of pulling himself up to the roof again.
10123{_}1971{_}And the hook was so small that there was no place for his other hand.
10123{_}1972{_}The only way he could cling to it at all was to grasp his wrist with the free hand as a partial relief from the strain upon his arm.
10123{_}1973{_}"Hold fast!"
10123{_}1974{_}called Patsy.
10123{_}1975{_}"I'm coming."
10123{_}1976{_}She sprang up the steps, through the boy's room and into the hallway.
10123{_}1977{_}There she quickly perceived the ladder, and mounted it to the roof.
10123{_}1978{_}Taking in the situation at a glance she ran with steady steps down the sloping roof to where the plank lay, and stepped out upon it far enough to see the boy dangling beside her.
10123{_}1979{_}Then she decided instantly what to do.
10123{_}1980{_}"Hang on!"
10123{_}1981{_}she called, and returning to the roof dragged the end of the plank to a position directly over the hook.
10123{_}1982{_}Then she lay flat upon it, an arm on either side of the plank, and reaching down seized one of the boy's wrists firmly in each hand.
10123{_}1983{_}"Now, then," said she, "let go the hook."
10123{_}1984{_}"If I do," answered the boy, his white face upturned to hers, "I'll drag you down with me."
10123{_}1985{_}"No you won't.
10123{_}1986{_}I'm very strong, and I'm sure I can save you.
10123{_}1987{_}Let go," she said, imperatively.
10123{_}1988{_}"I'm not afraid to die," replied the boy, his voice full of bitterness.
10123{_}1989{_}"Take away your hands, and I'll drop."
10123{_}1990{_}But Patsy gripped him more firmly than ever.
10123{_}1991{_}"Don't be a fool!"
10123{_}1992{_}she cried.
10123{_}1993{_}"There's no danger whatever, if you do just what I tell you."
10123{_}1994{_}His eyes met hers in a mute appeal; but suddenly he gained confidence, and resolved to trust her.
10123{_}1995{_}In any event, he could not cling to the hook much longer.
10123{_}1996{_}He released his hold, and swung in mid-air just beneath the plank, where the girl lay holding him by his wrists.
10123{_}1997{_}"Now, then," she said, quietly, "when I lift you up, grab the edges of the plank."
10123{_}1998{_}Patricia's strength was equal to her courage, and under the excitement of that desperate moment she did what few other girls of her size could ever have accomplished.
10123{_}1999{_}She drew the boy up until his eager hands caught the edges of the plank, and gripped it firmly.
10123{_}2000{_}Then she released him and crept a little back toward the roof.
10123{_}2001{_}"Now swing your legs up and you're safe!"
10123{_}2002{_}she cried.
10123{_}2003{_}He tried to obey, but his strength was failing him, and he could do no more than touch the plank with his toes.
10123{_}2004{_}"Once more," called the girl.
10123{_}2005{_}This time she caught his feet as they swung upward, and drew his legs around the plank.
10123{_}2006{_}"Can you climb up, now?"
10123{_}2007{_}she asked, anxiously.
10123{_}2008{_}"I'll try," he panted.
10123{_}2009{_}The plank upon which this little tragedy was being enacted was in full view of the small garden where Aunt Jane loved to sit in her chair and enjoy the flowers and the sunshine.
10123{_}2010{_}She could not see Kenneth's wing at all, but she could see the elevated plank leading from the roof to the oak tree, and for several days had been puzzled by its appearance and wondered for what purpose it was there.
10123{_}2011{_}Today, as she sat talking with John Merrick and Silas Watson, she suddenly gave a cry of surprise, and following her eyes the two men saw Kenneth step out upon the roof, fall, and slide over the edge.
10123{_}2012{_}For a moment all three remained motionless, seized with fear and consternation, and then they saw Patsy appear and run down to the plank.
10123{_}2013{_}This they watched her move, and saw her lie down upon it.
10123{_}2014{_}"She's trying to save him--he must be caught somewhere!"
10123{_}2015{_}cried the lawyer, and both men started at full speed to reach the spot by the round-about paths through the garden.
10123{_}2016{_}Aunt Jane sat still and watched.
10123{_}2017{_}Suddenly the form of the boy swung into view beneath the plank, dangling from the girl's outstretched arms.
10123{_}2018{_}The woman caught her breath, wondering what would happen next.
10123{_}2019{_}Patricia drew him up, until he seized the plank with his hands.
10123{_}2020{_}Then the girl crept back a little, and as the boy swung his feet upward she caught them and twined his legs over the plank.
10123{_}2021{_}And now came the supreme struggle.
10123{_}2022{_}The girl could do little more to help him.
10123{_}2023{_}He must manage to clamber upon the top of the plank himself.
10123{_}2024{_}Ordinarily Kenneth might have done this easily; but now his nerves were all unstrung, and he was half exhausted by the strain of the past few minutes.
10123{_}2025{_}Almost he did it; but not quite.
10123{_}2026{_}The next effort would be even weaker.
10123{_}2027{_}But now Patricia walked out upon the plank and Aunt Jane saw her lean down, grasp the boy's collar and drag him into a position of safety.
10123{_}2028{_}"Bravely done!"
10123{_}2029{_}she murmured, but even as the sound came from her lips the girl upon the bridge seemed in the exertion of the struggle to lose her balance.
10123{_}2030{_}She threw out her arms, leaned sidewise, and then fell headlong into the chasm and disappeared from view.
10123{_}2031{_}Aunt Jane's agonized scream brought Phibbs running to her side.
10123{_}2032{_}At a glance she saw that her mistress had fainted, and looking hastily around to discover the cause she observed the boy crawl slowly across the plank, reach the tree, and slide down its trunk to pass out of view behind the high hedge.
10123{_}2033{_}"Drat the boy!"
10123{_}2034{_}growled the old servant, angrily, "he'll be the death of Miss Jane, yet."
10123{_}2035{_}CHAPTER XVI.
10123{_}2036{_}GOOD RESULTS.
10123{_}2037{_}Uncle John could not run so swiftly as the lawyer, but he broke through a gap in the hedge and arrived at a point just beneath the plank at the same time that Silas Watson did.
10123{_}2038{_}One glance showed them the boy safely perched on top of the plank, but the girl was bending backward.
10123{_}2039{_}She threw out her arms in a vain endeavor to save herself, and with a low cry toppled and plunged swiftly toward the ground.
10123{_}2040{_}There was little time for the men to consider their actions.
10123{_}2041{_}Involuntarily they tried to catch Patricia, whose body struck them sharply, felling them to the ground, and then bounded against the hedge and back to the pavement.
10123{_}2042{_}When, half dazed, they scrambled to their feet, the girl lay motionless before them, a stream of red blood welling from a deep cut in her forhead, her eyes closed as if in sleep.
10123{_}2043{_}A moment more and the boy was kneeling beside her, striving to stay the bleeding with his handkerchief.
10123{_}2044{_}"Do something!
10123{_}2045{_}For God's sake try to do something," he wailed, piteously.
10123{_}2046{_}"Can't you see she's killed herself to save me?"
10123{_}2047{_}Uncle John knelt down and took the still form in his arms.
10123{_}2048{_}"Quiet, my lad," he said.
10123{_}2049{_}"She isn't dead.
10123{_}2050{_}Get Nora, and fetch the doctor as soon as you can."
10123{_}2051{_}The boy was gone instantly, his agony relieved by the chance of action, and followed by the lawyer, Uncle John carried his niece to the rose chamber and laid her upon her white bed.
10123{_}2052{_}Misery met them, then, and following her came Louise and Beth, full of horror and pity for the victim of the dreadful accident.
10123{_}2053{_}Jane Merrick had promptly recovered consciousness, for fainting spells were foreign to her nature.
10123{_}2054{_}Her first words to Phibbs, who was bending over her, were:  "Is she dead?"
10123{_}2055{_}"Who, Miss Jane?"
10123{_}2056{_}"Patricia."
10123{_}2057{_}"I don't know, Miss Jane.
10123{_}2058{_}Why should she be dead?"
10123{_}2059{_}"Run, you idiot!
10123{_}2060{_}Run at once and find out.
10123{_}2061{_}Ask my brother--ask anyone--if Patricia is dead!"
10123{_}2062{_}And so Phibbs came to the rose chamber and found the little group bending over the girl's unconscious form.
10123{_}2063{_}"Is she dead, sir?
10123{_}2064{_}Miss Jane wants to know," said the old servant, in awe-struck tones.
10123{_}2065{_}"No," answered Uncle John, gravely.
10123{_}2066{_}"She isn't dead, I'm sure; but I can't tell how badly she is hurt.
10123{_}2067{_}One of her legs--the right one--is broken, I know, for I felt it as I carried the child in my arms; but we must wait until the doctor comes before I can tell more."
10123{_}2068{_}Misery was something of a nurse, it seemed, and with the assistance of Louise, who proved most helpful in the emergency, she bathed the wound in the girl's forehead and bandaged it as well as she was able.
10123{_}2069{_}Between them the women also removed Patricia's clothing and got her into bed, where she lay white and still unconscious, but breathing so softly that they knew she was yet alive.
10123{_}2070{_}The doctor was not long in arriving, for Kenneth forced him to leap upon Nora's back and race away to Elmhurst, while the boy followed as swiftly as he could on the doctor's sober cob.
10123{_}2071{_}Dr. Eliel was only a country practitioner, but his varied experiences through many years had given him a practical knowledge of surgery, and after a careful examination of Patricia's injuries he was able to declare that she would make a fine recovery.
10123{_}2072{_}"Her leg is fractured, and she's badly bruised," he reported to Aunt Jane, who sent for him as soon as he could leave the sick room.
10123{_}2073{_}"But I do not think she has suffered any internal injuries, and the wound on her forehead is a mere nothing.
10123{_}2074{_}So, with good care, I expect the young lady to get along nicely."
10123{_}2075{_}"Do everything you can for her," said the woman, earnestly.
10123{_}2076{_}"You shall be well paid, Dr.
10123{_}2077{_}Eliel."
10123{_}2078{_}Before Patricia recovered her senses the doctor had sewn up her forehead and set the fractured limb, so that she suffered little pain from the first.
10123{_}2079{_}Louise and Beth hovered over her constantly, ministering to every possible want and filled with tenderest sympathy for their injured cousin.
10123{_}2080{_}The accident seemed to draw them out of their selfishness and petty intrigues and discovered in them the true womanly qualities that had lurked beneath the surface.
10123{_}2081{_}Patsy was not allowed to talk, but she smiled gratefully at her cousins, and the three girls seemed suddenly drawn nearer together than any of them would have thought possible a few hours before.
10123{_}2082{_}The boy paced constantly up and down outside Patricia's door, begging everyone who left the room, for news of the girl's condition.
10123{_}2083{_}All his reserve and fear of women seemed to have melted away as if by magic.
10123{_}2084{_}Even Beth and Louise were questioned eagerly, and they, having learned the story of Patricia's brave rescue of the boy, were very gentle with him and took pains not to frighten or offend him.
10123{_}2085{_}Toward evening Louise asked Patricia if she would see Kenneth for a moment, and the girl nodded a ready assent.
10123{_}2086{_}He came in awkward and trembling, glancing fearfully at the bandaged forehead and the still white face.
10123{_}2087{_}But Patricia managed to smile reassuringly, and held out a little hand for him to take.
10123{_}2088{_}The boy grasped it in both his own, and held it for several minutes while he stood motionless beside her, his wide eyes fixed intently upon her own.
10123{_}2089{_}Then Louise sent him away, and he went to his room and wept profusely, and then quieted down into a sort of dull stupor.
10123{_}2090{_}The next morning Uncle John dragged him away from Patricia's door and forced him to play chess.
10123{_}2091{_}The boy lost every game, being inattentive and absorbed in thought, until finally Uncle John gave up the attempt to amuse him and settled himself on the top stair for a quiet smoke.
10123{_}2092{_}The boy turned to the table, and took a sheet of paper from the drawer.
10123{_}2093{_}For an hour, perhaps, neither of these curious friends spoke a word, but at the end of that time Uncle John arose and knocked the ashes from his pipe.
10123{_}2094{_}Kenneth did not notice him.
10123{_}2095{_}The man approached the table and looked over the boy's shoulder, uttering an exclamation of surprise.
10123{_}2096{_}Upon the paper appeared a cleverly drawn pencil sketch of Patricia lying in her bed, a faint smile upon her face and her big blue eyes turned pleasantly upon a shadowy form that stood beside her holding her hand.
10123{_}2097{_}The likeness was admirable, and if there were faults in the perspective and composition Uncle John did not recognize them.
10123{_}2098{_}He gave a low whistle and turned thoughtfully away, and the young artist was so absorbed that he did not even look up.
10123{_}2099{_}Strolling away to the stables, Uncle John met old Donald, who enquired:  "How is Miss Patsy this morning, sir?"
10123{_}2100{_}It was the name she had given, and preferred to be called by.
10123{_}2101{_}"She's doing finely," said Uncle John.
10123{_}2102{_}"A brave girl, sir!"
10123{_}2103{_}"Yes, Donald."
10123{_}2104{_}"And the boy?"
10123{_}2105{_}"Why, he seems changed, in some way, Donald.
10123{_}2106{_}Not so nervous and wild as usual, you know.
10123{_}2107{_}I've just left him drawing a picture.
10123{_}2108{_}Curious.
10123{_}2109{_}A good picture, too."
10123{_}2110{_}"Ah, he can do that, sir, as well as a real artist."
10123{_}2111{_}"Have you known him to draw, before this?"
10123{_}2112{_}"Why, he's always at it, sir, in his quieter moods.
10123{_}2113{_}I've got a rare good likeness o' myself, as he did long ago, in the harness-room."
10123{_}2114{_}"May I see it?"
10123{_}2115{_}"With pleasure, sir."
10123{_}2116{_}Donald led the way to the harness-room, and took from the cupboard the precious board he had so carefully preserved.
10123{_}2117{_}Uncle John glanced at it and laughed aloud.
10123{_}2118{_}He could well appreciate the humor of the sketch, which Donald never had understood, and the caricature was as clever as it was amusing.
10123{_}2119{_}He handed the treasure back to Donald and went away even more thoughtful than before.
10123{_}2120{_}A few days later a large package arrived at Elmhurst addressed to Kenneth Forbes, and Oscar carried it at once to the boy's room, who sat for an hour looking at it in silent amazement.
10123{_}2121{_}Then he carefully unwrapped it, and found it to contain a portable easel, a quantity of canvas and drawing-paper, paints and oils of every description (mostly all unknown to him) and pencils, brushes and water colors in profusion.
10123{_}2122{_}Kenneth's heart bounded with joy.
10123{_}2123{_}Here was wealth, indeed, greater than he had ever hoped for.
10123{_}2124{_}He puzzled his brain for weeks to discover how this fairy gift had ever come to him, but he was happier in its possession than he had ever been before in all his life.
10123{_}2125{_}Patricia improved rapidly.
10123{_}2126{_}Had it not been for the broken leg she would have been out of the house in a week, as good as ever; but broken limbs take time to heal, and Dr. Eliel would not permit the girl to leave her bed until ten days had passed.
10123{_}2127{_}Meantime everyone delighted to attend her.
10123{_}2128{_}Louise and Beth sat with her for hours, reading or working, for the rose chamber was cheery and pleasant, and its big windows opened upon the prettiest part of the gardens.
10123{_}2129{_}The two girls were even yet suspicious of one another, each striving to win an advantage with Aunt Jane; but neither had the slightest fear that Patricia would ever interfere with their plans.
10123{_}2130{_}So they allowed their natural inclinations to pet and admire the heroine of the hour full sway, and Patsy responded so sweetly and frankly to their advances that they came to love her dearly, and wondered why they had not discovered from the first how lovable their Irish cousin could be.
10123{_}2131{_}Kenneth, also came daily to the sick room for a visit, and Patsy had a way of drawing the boy out and making him talk that was really irresistible.
10123{_}2132{_}After his fairy gift arrived he could not help telling the girls all about it and then he brought the things down and displayed them, and promised Patsy he would make a picture of the garden for her.
10123{_}2133{_}Then, after the girl got better, he brought his easel down to her room, where she could watch him work, and began upon the picture, while the cousins joined him in speculations as to who the mysterious donor could he.
10123{_}2134{_}"At first," said Kenneth, "I thought it was Mr. Watson, for he's alway been very good to me; but he says he knows nothing about it.
10123{_}2135{_}Then I though it might be Uncle John; but Uncle John is too poor to afford such an expensive present."
10123{_}2136{_}"I don't believe he has a penny in the world," said Louise, who sat by with some needle-work.
10123{_}2137{_}"All he owns," remarked Beth, with a laugh, "is an extra necktie, slightly damaged."
10123{_}2138{_}"But he's a dear old man," said Patsy, loyally, "and I'm sure he would have given all those things to Kenneth had he been able."
10123{_}2139{_}"Then who was it?"
10123{_}2140{_}asked the boy.
10123{_}2141{_}"Why, Aunt Jane, to be sure," declared Patsy.
10123{_}2142{_}The boy scowled, and shook his head.
10123{_}2143{_}"She wouldn't do anything to please me, even to save her life," he growled.
10123{_}2144{_}"She hates me, I know that well enough."
10123{_}2145{_}"Oh, no; I'm sure she doesn't," said Patsy.
10123{_}2146{_}"Aunt Jane has a heap of good in her; but you've got to dig for it, like you do for gold.
10123{_}2147{_}'Twould be just like her to make you this present and keep it a secret."
10123{_}2148{_}"If she really did it," replied the boy, slowly, "and it seems as if she is the only one.
10123{_}2149{_}I know who could afford such a gift, it stands to reason that either Uncle John or Mr. Watson asked her to, and she did it to please them.
10123{_}2150{_}I've lived here for years, and she has never spoken a kindly word to me or done me a kindly act.
10123{_}2151{_}It isn't likely she'd begin now, is it?"
10123{_}2152{_}Unable to make a reassuring reply, Patsy remained silent, and the boy went on with his work.
10123{_}2153{_}He first outlined the picture in pencil, and then filled it in with water color.
10123{_}2154{_}They all expressed admiration for the drawing; but the color effect was so horrible that even Patsy found no words to praise it, and the boy in a fit of sudden anger tore the thing to shreds and so destroyed it.
10123{_}2155{_}"But I must have my picture, anyhow," said the girl.
10123{_}2156{_}"Make it in pen and ink or pencil, Ken.
10123{_}2157{_}and I'm sure it will be beautiful."
10123{_}2158{_}"You need instruction, to do water color properly," suggested Louise.
10123{_}2159{_}"Then I can never do it," he replied, bitterly.
10123{_}2160{_}But he adopted Patsy's suggestion and sketched the garden very prettily in pen and ink.
10123{_}2161{_}By the time the second picture was completed Patsy had received permission to leave her room, which she did in Aunt Jane's second-best wheel chair.
10123{_}2162{_}Her first trip was to Aunt Jane's own private garden, where the invalid, who had not seen her niece since the accident, had asked her to come.
10123{_}2163{_}Patsy wanted Kenneth to wheel her, but the boy, with a touch of his old surly demeanor, promptly refused to meet Jane Merrick face to face.
10123{_}2164{_}So Beth wheeled the chair and Louise walked by Patsy's side, and soon the three nieces reached their aunt's retreat.
10123{_}2165{_}Aunt Jane was not in an especially amiable mood.
10123{_}2166{_}"Well, girl, how do you like being a fool?"
10123{_}2167{_}she demanded, as Patsy's chair came to a stand just opposite her own.
10123{_}2168{_}"It feels so natural that I don't mind it," replied Patsy, laughing.
10123{_}2169{_}"You might have killed yourself, and all for nothing," continued the old woman, querulously.
10123{_}2170{_}Patsy looked at her pityingly.
10123{_}2171{_}Her aunt's face had aged greatly in the two weeks, and the thin gray hair seemed now almost white.
10123{_}2172{_}"Are you feeling better, dear?"
10123{_}2173{_}asked the girl.
10123{_}2174{_}"I shall never be better," said Jane Merrick, sternly.
10123{_}2175{_}"The end is not far off now."
10123{_}2176{_}"Oh, I'm sorry to hear you say that!"
10123{_}2177{_}said Patsy; "but I hope it is not true.
10123{_}2178{_}Why, here are we four newly found relations all beginning to get acquainted, and to love one another, and we can't have our little party broken up, auntie dear."
10123{_}2179{_}"Five of us--five relations," cried Uncle John, coming around the corner of the hedge.
10123{_}2180{_}"Don't I count, Patsy, you rogue?
10123{_}2181{_}Why you're looking as bright and as bonny as can be.
10123{_}2182{_}I wouldn't be surprised if you could toddle."
10123{_}2183{_}"Not yet," she answered, cheerfully.
10123{_}2184{_}"But I'm doing finely, Uncle John, and it won't be long before I can get about as well as ever."
10123{_}2185{_}"And to think," said Aunt Jane, bitterly, "that all this trouble was caused by that miserable boy!
10123{_}2186{_}If I knew where to send him he'd not stay at Elmhurst a day longer."
10123{_}2187{_}"Why, he's my best friend, aunt," announced Patsy, quietly.
10123{_}2188{_}"I don't think I could be happy at Elmhurst without Kenneth."
10123{_}2189{_}"He has quite reformed," said Louise, "and seems like a very nice boy."
10123{_}2190{_}"He's a little queer, yet, at times," added Beth, "but not a bit rude, as he used to be."
10123{_}2191{_}Aunt Jane looked from one to the other in amazement.
10123{_}2192{_}No one had spoken so kindly of the boy before in years.
10123{_}2193{_}And Uncle John, with a thoughtful look on his face, said slowly:  "The fact is, Jane, you've never given the boy a chance.
10123{_}2194{_}On the contrary, you nearly ruined him by making a hermit of him and giving him no schooling to speak of and no society except that of servants.
10123{_}2195{_}He was as wild as a hawk when I first came, but these girls are just the sort of companions he needs, to soften him and make him a man.
10123{_}2196{_}I've no doubt he'll come out all right, in the end."
10123{_}2197{_}"Perhaps you'd like to adopt him yourself, John," sneered the woman, furious at this praise of the one person she so greatly disliked.
10123{_}2198{_}Her brother drew his hands from his pockets, looked around in a helpless and embarrassed way, and then tried fumblingly to fill his pipe.
10123{_}2199{_}"I ain't in the adopting business, Jane," he answered meekly.
10123{_}2200{_}"And if I was," with a quaint smile, "I'd adopt one or two of these nieces o' mine, instead of Tom Bradley's nephew.
10123{_}2201{_}If Bradley hadn't seen you, Jane, and loved your pretty face when you were young, Kenneth Forbes would now be the owner of Elmhurst.
10123{_}2202{_}Did you ever think of that?"
10123{_}2203{_}Did she ever think of it?
10123{_}2204{_}Why, it was this very fact that made the boy odious to her.
10123{_}2205{_}The woman grew white with rage.
10123{_}2206{_}"John Merrick, leave my presence."
10123{_}2207{_}"All right, Jane."
10123{_}2208{_}He stopped to light his pipe, and then slowly walked away, leaving an embarrassed group behind him.
10123{_}2209{_}Patsy, however, was equal to the occasion.
10123{_}2210{_}She began at once to chatter about Dr. Eliel, and the scar that would always show on her forehead; and how surprised the Major, her father, would be when he returned from the visit to his colonel and found his daughter had been through the wars herself, and bore the evidence of honorable wounds.
10123{_}2211{_}Louise gracefully assisted her cousin to draw Aunt Jane into a more genial mood, and between them they presently succeeded.
10123{_}2212{_}The interview that had begun so unfortunately ended quite pleasantly, and when Patricia returned to her room her aunt bade her adieu almost tenderly.
10123{_}2213{_}"In fact," said Louise to Beth, in the privacy of the latter's chamber, "I'm getting rather worried over Aunt Jane's evident weakness for our Cousin Patsy.
10123{_}2214{_}Once or twice today I caught a look in her eye when she looked at Patsy that she has never given either you or me.
10123{_}2215{_}The Irish girl may get the money yet."
10123{_}2216{_}"Nonsense," said Beth.
10123{_}2217{_}"She has said she wouldn't accept a penny of it, and I'm positive she'll keep her word."
10123{_}2218{_}CHAPTER XVII.
10123{_}2219{_}AUNT JANE'S HEIRESS.
10123{_}2220{_}"Silas," said Aunt Jane to her lawyer, the next morning after her interview with Patsy, "I'm ready to have you draw up my will."
10123{_}2221{_}Mr. Watson gave a start of astonishment.
10123{_}2222{_}In his own mind he had arrived at the conclusion that the will would never be executed, and to have Miss Merrick thus suddenly declare her decision was enough to startle even the lawyer's natural reserve.
10123{_}2223{_}"Very well, Jane," he said, briefly.
10123{_}2224{_}They were alone in the invalid's morning room, Phibbs having been asked to retire.
10123{_}2225{_}"There is no use disguising the fact, Silas, that I grow weaker every day, and the numbness is creeping nearer and nearer to my heart," said Miss Merrick, in her usual even tones.
10123{_}2226{_}"It is folly for me to trifle with these few days of grace yet allowed me, and I have fully made up my mind as to the disposition of my property."
10123{_}2227{_}"Yes?"
10123{_}2228{_}he said, enquiringly, and drew from his pocket a pencil and paper.
10123{_}2229{_}"I shall leave to my niece Louise five thousand dollars."
10123{_}2230{_}"Yes, Jane," jotting down the memorandum.
10123{_}2231{_}"And to Elizabeth a like sum."
10123{_}2232{_}The lawyer seemed disappointed.
10123{_}2233{_}He tapped the pencil against his teeth, musingly, for a moment, and then wrote down the amount.
10123{_}2234{_}"Also to my brother, John Merrick, the sum of five thousand dollars," she resumed.
10123{_}2235{_}"To your brother?"
10123{_}2236{_}"Yes.
10123{_}2237{_}That should be enough to take care of him as long as he lives.
10123{_}2238{_}He seems quite simple in his tastes, and he is an old man."
10123{_}2239{_}The lawyer wrote it down.
10123{_}2240{_}"All my other remaining property, both real and personal, I shall leave to my niece, Patricia Doyle."
10123{_}2241{_}"Jane!"
10123{_}2242{_}"Did you hear me?"
10123{_}2243{_}"Yes."
10123{_}2244{_}"Then do as I bid you, Silas Watson."
10123{_}2245{_}He leaned back in his chair and looked at her thoughtfully.
10123{_}2246{_}"I am not only your lawyer, Jane; I am also your friend and counsellor.
10123{_}2247{_}Do you realize what this bequest means?"
10123{_}2248{_}he asked, gently.
10123{_}2249{_}"It means that Patricia will inherit Elmhurst--and a fortune besides.
10123{_}2250{_}Why not, Silas?
10123{_}2251{_}I liked the child from the first.
10123{_}2252{_}She's frank and open and brave, and will do credit to my judgment."
10123{_}2253{_}"She is very young and unsophisticated," said the lawyer, "and of all your nieces she will least appreciate your generosity."
10123{_}2254{_}"You are to be my executor, and manage the estate until the girl comes of age.
10123{_}2255{_}You will see that she is properly educated and fitted for her station in life.
10123{_}2256{_}As for appreciation, or gratitude, I don't care a snap of my finger for such fol-de-rol."
10123{_}2257{_}The lawyer sighed.
10123{_}2258{_}"But the boy, Jane?
10123{_}2259{_}You seem to have forgotten him," he said.
10123{_}2260{_}"Drat the boy!
10123{_}2261{_}I've done enough for him already."
10123{_}2262{_}"Wouldn't Tom like you to provide for Kenneth in some way, however humbly?"
10123{_}2263{_}She glared at him angrily.
10123{_}2264{_}"How do you know what Tom would like, after all these years?"
10123{_}2265{_}she asked, sternly.
10123{_}2266{_}"And how should I know, either?
10123{_}2267{_}The money is mine, and the boy is nothing to me.
10123{_}2268{_}Let him shift for himself."
10123{_}2269{_}"There is a great deal of money, Jane," declared the lawyer, impressively.
10123{_}2270{_}"We have been fortunate in our investments, and you have used but little of your ample income.
10123{_}2271{_}To spare fifty thousand dollars to Kenneth, who is Tom's sole remaining relative, would be no hardship to Patricia.
10123{_}2272{_}Indeed, she would scarcely miss it."
10123{_}2273{_}"You remind me of something, Silas," she said, looking at him with friendly eyes.
10123{_}2274{_}"Make a memorandum of twenty thousand dollars to Silas Watson.
10123{_}2275{_}You have been very faithful to my interests and have helped materially to increase my fortune."
10123{_}2276{_}"Thank you, Jane."
10123{_}2277{_}He wrote down the amount as calmly as he had done the others.
10123{_}2278{_}"And the boy?"
10123{_}2279{_}he asked, persistently.
10123{_}2280{_}Aunt Jane sighed wearily, and leaned against her pillows.
10123{_}2281{_}"Give the boy two thousand," she said.
10123{_}2282{_}"Make it ten, Jane."
10123{_}2283{_}"I'll make it five, and not a penny more," she rejoined.
10123{_}2284{_}"Now leave me, and prepare the paper at once.
10123{_}2285{_}I want to sign it today, if possible."
10123{_}2286{_}He bowed gravely, and left the room.
10123{_}2287{_}Toward evening the lawyer came again, bringing with him a notary from the village.
10123{_}2288{_}Dr. Eliel, who had come to visit Patricia, was also called into Jane Merrick's room, and after she had carefully read the paper in their presence the mistress of Elmhurst affixed her signature to the document which transferred the great estate to the little Irish girl, and the notary and the doctor solemnly witnessed it and retired.
10123{_}2289{_}"Now, Silas," said the old woman, with a sigh of intense relief, "I can die in peace."
10123{_}2290{_}Singularly enough, the signing of the will seemed not to be the end for Jane Merrick, but the beginning of an era of unusual comfort.
10123{_}2291{_}On the following morning she awakened brighter than usual, having passed a good night, freed from the worries and anxieties that had beset her for weeks.
10123{_}2292{_}She felt more like her old self than at any time since the paralysis had overtaken her, and passed the morning most enjoyably in her sunshiney garden.
10123{_}2293{_}Here Patricia was also brought in her wheel chair by Beth, who then left the two invalids together.
10123{_}2294{_}They conversed genially enough, for a time, until an unfortunate remark of Aunt Jane's which seemed to asperse her father's character aroused Patricia's ire.
10123{_}2295{_}Then she loosened her tongue, and in her voluable Irish way berated her aunt until poor Phibbs stood aghast at such temerity, and even Mr. Watson, who arrived to enquire after his client and friend, was filled with amazement.
10123{_}2296{_}He cast a significant look at Miss Merrick, who answered it in her usual emphatic way.
10123{_}2297{_}"Patricia is quite right, Silas," she declared, "and I deserve all that she has said.
10123{_}2298{_}If the girl were fond enough of me to defend me as heartily as she does her father, I would be very proud, indeed."
10123{_}2299{_}Patricia cooled at once, and regarded her aunt with a sunny smile.
10123{_}2300{_}"Forgive me!"
10123{_}2301{_}she begged.
10123{_}2302{_}"I know you did not mean it, and I was wrong to talk to you in such a way."
10123{_}2303{_}So harmony was restored, and Mr. Watson wondered more and more at this strange perversion of the old woman's character.
10123{_}2304{_}Heretofore any opposition had aroused in her intense rage and a fierce antagonism, but now she seemed delighted to have Patsy fly at her, and excused the girl's temper instead of resenting it.
10123{_}2305{_}But Patsy was a little ashamed of herself this morning, realizing perhaps that Aunt Jane had been trying to vex her, just to enjoy her indignant speeches; and she also realized the fact that her aunt was old and suffering, and not wholly responsible for her aggravating and somewhat malicious observations.
10123{_}2306{_}So she firmly resolved not to be so readily entrapped again, and was so bright and cheery during the next hour that Aunt Jane smiled more than once, and at one time actually laughed at her niece's witty repartee.
10123{_}2307{_}After that it became the daily program for Patsy to spend her mornings in Aunt Jane's little garden, and although they sometimes clashed, and, as Phibbs told Beth, "had dreadful fights," they both enjoyed these hours very much.
10123{_}2308{_}The two girls became rather uneasy during the days their cousin spent in the society of Aunt Jane.
10123{_}2309{_}Even the dreadful accounts they received from Phibbs failed wholly to reassure them, and Louise redoubled her solicitious attentions to her aunt in order to offset the influence Patricia seemed to be gaining over her.
10123{_}2310{_}Louise had also become, by this time, the managing housekeeper of the establishment, and it was certain that Aunt Jane looked upon her eldest and most competent niece with much favor.
10123{_}2311{_}Beth, with all her friends to sing her praises, seemed to make less headway with her aunt than either of the others, and gradually she sank into a state of real despondency.
10123{_}2312{_}"I've done the best I could," she wrote her mother, "but I'm not as clever as Louise nor as amusing as Patricia; so Aunt Jane pays little attention to me.
10123{_}2313{_}She's a dreadful old woman, and I can't bring myself to appear to like her.
10123{_}2314{_}That probably accounts for my failure; but I may as well stay on here until something happens."
10123{_}2315{_}In a fortnight more Patricia abandoned her chair and took to crutches, on which she hobbled everywhere as actively as the others walked.
10123{_}2316{_}She affected her cousins' society more, from this time, and Aunt Jane's society less, for she had come to be fond of the two girls who had nursed her so tenderly, and it was natural that a young girl would prefer to be with those of her own age rather than a crabbed old woman like Aunt Jane.
10123{_}2317{_}Kenneth also now became Patsy's faithful companion, for the boy had lost his former bashfulness and fear of girls, and had grown to feel at ease even in the society of Beth and Louise.
10123{_}2318{_}The four had many excursions and picnics into the country together; but Kenneth and Patsy were recognized as especial chums, and the other girls did not interfere in their friendship except to tease them, occasionally, in a good natured way.
10123{_}2319{_}The boy's old acquaintances could hardly recognize him as the same person they had known before Patricia's adventure on the plank.
10123{_}2320{_}His fits of gloomy abstraction and violent bursts of temper had alike vanished, or only prevailed at brief intervals.
10123{_}2321{_}Nor was he longer rude and unmannerly to those with whom he came in contact.
10123{_}2322{_}Awkward he still was, and lacking in many graces that education and good society can alone confer; but he was trying hard to be, as he confided to old Uncle John, "like other people," and succeeded in adapting himself very well to his new circumstances.
10123{_}2323{_}Although he had no teacher, as yet, he had begun to understand color a little, and succeeded in finishing one or two water-color sketches which Patsy, who knew nothing at all of such things, pronounced "wonderfully fine."
10123{_}2324{_}Of course the boy blushed with pleasure and was encouraged to still greater effort.
10123{_}2325{_}The girl was also responsible for Kenneth's sudden advancement in the household at Elmhurst.
10123{_}2326{_}One day she said calmly to Aunt Jane:  "I've invited Kenneth to dinner this evening."
10123{_}2327{_}The woman flew angry in an instant.
10123{_}2328{_}"Who gave you such authority?"
10123{_}2329{_}she demanded.
10123{_}2330{_}"No one.
10123{_}2331{_}I just took it," said Patsy, saucily.
10123{_}2332{_}"He shall not come," declared Aunt Jane, sternly.
10123{_}2333{_}"I'll have no interference from you, Miss, with my household arrangements.
10123{_}2334{_}Phibbs, call Louise!"
10123{_}2335{_}Patsy's brow grew dark.
10123{_}2336{_}Presently Louise appeared.
10123{_}2337{_}"Instruct the servants to forbid that boy to enter my dining room this evening," she said to Louise.
10123{_}2338{_}"Also, Louise," said Patsy, "tell them not to lay a plate for me, and ask Oscar to be ready with the wagon at five o'clock.
10123{_}2339{_}I'm going home."
10123{_}2340{_}Louise hesitated, and looked from Miss Jane to Patsy, and back again.
10123{_}2341{_}They were glaring upon each other like two gorgons.
10123{_}2342{_}Then she burst into laughter; she could not help it, the sight was too ridiculous.
10123{_}2343{_}A moment later Patsy was laughing, too, and then Aunt Jane allowed a grim smile to cross her features.
10123{_}2344{_}"Never mind, Louise," she said, with remarkable cheerfulness; "We'll compromise matters."
10123{_}2345{_}"How?"
10123{_}2346{_}asked Patsy.
10123{_}2347{_}"By putting a plate for Kenneth," said her aunt, cooly.
10123{_}2348{_}"I imagine I can stand his society for one evening."
10123{_}2349{_}So the matter was arranged to Patricia's satisfaction, and the boy came to dinner, trembling and unhappy at first, but soon placed at ease by the encouragements of the three girls.
10123{_}2350{_}Indeed, he behaved so well, in the main, and was so gentle and unobstrusive, that Aunt Jane looked at him with surprise, and favored him with one or two speeches which he answered modestly and well.
10123{_}2351{_}Patsy was radiant with delight, and the next day Aunt Jane remarked casually that she did not object to the boy's presence at dinner, at all, and he could come whenever he liked.
10123{_}2352{_}This arrangement gave great pleasure to both Uncle John and Mr. Watson, the latter of whom was often present at the "state dinner," and both men congratulated Patsy upon the distinct victory she had won.
10123{_}2353{_}No more was said about her leaving Elmhurst.
10123{_}2354{_}The Major wrote that he was having a splendid time with the colonel, and begged for an extension of his vacation, to which Patsy readily agreed, she being still unable on account of her limb to return to her work at Madam Borne's.
10123{_}2355{_}And so the days glided pleasantly by, and August came to find a happy company of young folks at old Elmhurst, with Aunt Jane wonderfully improved in health and Uncle John beaming complacently upon everyone he chanced to meet.
10123{_}2356{_}CHAPTER XVIII.
10123{_}2357{_}PATRICIA SPEAKS FRANKLY.
10123{_}2358{_}It was Lawyer Watson's suggestion that she was being unjust to Beth and Louise, in encouraging them to hope they might inherit Elmhurst, that finally decided Aunt Jane to end all misunderstandings and inform her nieces of the fact that she had made a final disposition of her property.
10123{_}2359{_}So one morning she sent word asking them all into her room, and when the nieces appeared they found Uncle John and the lawyer already in their aunt's presence.
10123{_}2360{_}There was an air of impressive formality pervading the room, although Miss Merrick's brother, at least, was as ignorant as her nieces of the reason why they had been summoned.
10123{_}2361{_}Patsy came in last, hobbling actively on her crutches, although the leg was now nearly recovered, and seated herself somewhat in the rear of the apartment.
10123{_}2362{_}Aunt Jane looked into one expectant face after another with curious interest, and then broke the silence by saying, gravely, but in more gentle tones than she was accustomed to use:  "I believe, young ladies, that you have understood from the first my strongest reason for inviting you to visit Elmhurst this summer.
10123{_}2363{_}I am old, and must soon pass away, and instead of leaving you and your parents, who would be my legitimate heirs, to squabble over my property when I am gone, I decided to excute a will bequeathing my estate to some one who would take proper care of it and maintain it in a creditable manner.
10123{_}2364{_}I had no personal acquaintance with any of you, but judged that one out of the three might serve my purpose, and therefore invited you all here."
10123{_}2365{_}By this time the hearts of Louise and Beth were fluttering with excitement, and even Patsy looked interested.
10123{_}2366{_}Uncle John sat a little apart, watching them with an amused smile upon his face, and the lawyer sat silent with his eyes fixed upon a pattern in the rug.
10123{_}2367{_}"In arriving at a decision, which I may say I have succeeded in doing," continued Aunt Jane, calmly, "I do not claim to have acted with either wisdom or discernment.
10123{_}2368{_}I have simply followed my own whim, as I have the right to do, and selected the niece I prefer to become my heiress.
10123{_}2369{_}You cannot accuse of injustice, because none of you had a right to expect anything of me; but I will say this, that I am well pleased with all three of you, and now wish that I had taken pains to form your acquaintance earlier in life.
10123{_}2370{_}You might have cheered my old age and rendered it less lonely and dull."
10123{_}2371{_}"Well said, Jane," remarked Uncle John, nodding his head approvingly.
10123{_}2372{_}She did not notice the interruption, but presently continued:  "Some days ago I asked my lawyer, Mr. Watson, to draw up my will.
10123{_}2373{_}It was at once prepared and signed, and now stands as my last will and testament.
10123{_}2374{_}I have given to you, Louise, the sum of five thousand dollars."
10123{_}2375{_}Louise laughed nervously, and threw out her hands with an indifferent gesture.
10123{_}2376{_}"Many thanks, Aunt," she said, lightly.
10123{_}2377{_}"To you, Beth," continued Miss Merrick, "I have given the same sum."
10123{_}2378{_}Beth's heart sank, and tears forced themselves into her eyes in spite of her efforts to restrain them.
10123{_}2379{_}She said nothing.
10123{_}2380{_}Aunt Jane turned to her brother.
10123{_}2381{_}"I have also provided for you, John, in the sum of five thousand dollars."
10123{_}2382{_}"Me!"
10123{_}2383{_}he exclaimed, astounded.
10123{_}2384{_}"Why, suguration, Jane, I don't--"  "Silence!"
10123{_}2385{_}she cried, sternly.
10123{_}2386{_}"I expect neither thanks nor protests.
10123{_}2387{_}If you take care of the money, John, it will last you as long as you live."
10123{_}2388{_}Uncle John laughed.
10123{_}2389{_}He doubled up in his chair and rocked back and forth, shaking his little round body as if he had met with the most amusing thing that had ever happened in his life.
10123{_}2390{_}Aunt Jane stared at him, while Louise and Beth looked their astonishment, but Patsy's clear laughter rang above Uncle John's gasping chuckles.
10123{_}2391{_}"I hope, dear Uncle," said she, mischievously, "that when poor Aunt Jane is gone you'll be able to buy a new necktie."
10123{_}2392{_}He looked at her whimsically, and wiped the tears from his eyes.
10123{_}2393{_}"Thank you, Jane," said the little man to his sister.
10123{_}2394{_}"It's a lot of money, and I'll be proud to own it."
10123{_}2395{_}"Why did you laugh."
10123{_}2396{_}demanded Aunt Jane.
10123{_}2397{_}"I just happened to think that our old Dad once said I'd never be worth a dollar in all my life.
10123{_}2398{_}What would he say now, Jane, if he knew I stood good to have five thousand--if I can manage to outlive you?"
10123{_}2399{_}She turned from him with an expression of scorn.
10123{_}2400{_}"In addition to these bequests," said she, "I have left five thousand to the boy and twenty thousand to Mr. Watson.
10123{_}2401{_}The remainder of the property will go to Patricia."
10123{_}2402{_}For a moment the room was intensely still.
10123{_}2403{_}Then Patricia said, with quiet determination:  "You may as well make another will, Aunt.
10123{_}2404{_}I'll not touch a penny of your money."
10123{_}2405{_}"Why not?"
10123{_}2406{_}asked the woman, almost fiercely.
10123{_}2407{_}"You have been kind to me, and you mean well," said Patricia.
10123{_}2408{_}"I would rather not tell you my reasons."
10123{_}2409{_}"I demand to know them!"
10123{_}2410{_}"Ah, aunt; can't you understand, without my speaking?"
10123{_}2411{_}"No," said the other; but a flush crossed her pale cheek, nevertheless.
10123{_}2412{_}Patsy arose and stumped to a position directly in front of Jane Merrick, where she rested on her crutches.
10123{_}2413{_}Her eyes were bright and full of indignation, and her plain little face was so white that every freckle showed distinctly.
10123{_}2414{_}"There was a time, years ago," she began in a low voice, "when you were very rich and your sister Violet, my mother, was very poor.
10123{_}2415{_}Her health was bad, and she had me to care for, while my father was very ill with a fever.
10123{_}2416{_}She was proud, too, and for herself she would never have begged a penny of anyone; but for my sake she asked her rich sister to loan her a little money to tide her over her period of want.
10123{_}2417{_}What did you do, Jane Merrick, you who lived in a beautiful mansion, and had more money than you could use?
10123{_}2418{_}You insulted her, telling her she belonged to a family of beggars, and that none of them could wheedle your money away from you!"
10123{_}2419{_}"It was true," retorted the elder woman, stubbornly.
10123{_}2420{_}"They were after me like a drove of wolves--every Merrick of them all--and they would have ruined me if I had let them bleed me as they wished."
10123{_}2421{_}"So far as my mother is concerned, that's a lie," said Patsy, quietly.
10123{_}2422{_}"She never appealed to you but that once, but worked as bravely as she could to earn money in her own poor way.
10123{_}2423{_}The result was that she died, and I was left to the care of strangers until my father was well enough to support me."
10123{_}2424{_}She paused, and again the room seemed unnaturally still.
10123{_}2425{_}"I'm sorry, girl," said Aunt Jane, at last, in trembling tones.
10123{_}2426{_}"I was wrong.
10123{_}2427{_}I see it now, and I am sorry I refused Violet."
10123{_}2428{_}"Then I forgive you!"
10123{_}2429{_}said Patsy, impulsively.
10123{_}2430{_}"I forgive you all, Aunt Jane; for through your own selfishness you cut yourself off from all your family--from all who might have loved you--and you have lived all these years a solitary and loveless life.
10123{_}2431{_}There'll be no grudge of mine to follow you to the grave, Aunt Jane.
10123{_}2432{_}But," her voice hardening, "I'll never touch a penny of the money that was denied my poor dead mother.
10123{_}2433{_}Thank God the old Dad and I are independent, and can earn our own living."
10123{_}2434{_}Uncle John came to where Patsy stood and put both arms around her, pressing her--crutches and all--close to his breast.
10123{_}2435{_}Then he released her, and without a word stalked from the room.
10123{_}2436{_}"Leave me, now," said Aunt Jane, in a husky voice.
10123{_}2437{_}"I want time to think."
10123{_}2438{_}Patricia hobbled forward, placed one hand caressingly upon the gray head, and then bent and kissed Aunt Jane's withered cheek.
10123{_}2439{_}"That's right," she whispered.
10123{_}2440{_}"Think it over, dear.
10123{_}2441{_}It's all past and done, now, and I'm sorry I had to hurt you.
10123{_}2442{_}But--not a penny, aunt--remember, not a penny will I take!"
10123{_}2443{_}Then she left the room, followed by Louise and Beth, both of whom were glad to be alone that they might conquer their bitter disappointment.
10123{_}2444{_}Louise, however, managed to accept the matter philosophically, as the following extract from her letter to her mother will prove:  "After all, it isn't so bad as it might be, mater, dear," she wrote.
10123{_}2445{_}"I'll get five thousand, at the very worst, and that will help us on our way considerably.
10123{_}2446{_}But I am quite sure that Patsy means just what she says, and that she will yet induce Aunt Jane to alter her will.
10123{_}2447{_}In that case I believe the estate will either be divided between Beth and me, or I will get it all.
10123{_}2448{_}Anyway, I shall stay here and play my best cards until the game is finished."
10123{_}2449{_}CHAPTER XIX.
10123{_}2450{_}DUPLICITY.
10123{_}2451{_}Aunt Jane had a bad night, as might have been expected after her trials of the previous day.
10123{_}2452{_}She sent for Patricia early in the forenoon, and when the girl arrived she was almost shocked by the change in her aunt's appearance.
10123{_}2453{_}The invalid's face seemed drawn and gray, and she lay upon her cushions breathing heavily and without any appearance of vitality or strength.
10123{_}2454{_}Even the sharpness and piercing quality of her hard gray eyes was lacking and the glance she cast at her niece was rather pleading than defiant.
10123{_}2455{_}"I want you to reconsider your decision of yesterday, Patricia," she begun.
10123{_}2456{_}"Don't ask me to do that, aunt," replied the girl, firmly.
10123{_}2457{_}"My mind is fully made up."
10123{_}2458{_}"I have made mistakes, I know," continued the woman feebly; "but I want to do the right thing, at last."
10123{_}2459{_}"Then I will show you how," said Patricia, quickly.
10123{_}2460{_}"You mustn't think me impertinent, aunt, for I don't mean to be so at all.
10123{_}2461{_}But tell me; why did you wish to leave me your money?"
10123{_}2462{_}"Because your nature is quite like my own, child, and I admire your independence and spirit."
10123{_}2463{_}"But my cousins are much more deserving," said she, thoughtfully.
10123{_}2464{_}"Louise is very sweet and amiable, and loves you more than I do, while Beth is the most sensible and practical girl I have ever known."
10123{_}2465{_}"It may be so," returned Aunt Jane, impatiently; "but I have left each a legacy, Patricia, and you alone are my choice for the mistress of Elmhurst.
10123{_}2466{_}I told you yesterday I should not try to be just.
10123{_}2467{_}I mean to leave my property according to my personal desire, and no one shall hinder me."
10123{_}2468{_}This last with a spark of her old vigor.
10123{_}2469{_}"But that is quite wrong, aunt, and if you desire me to inherit your wealth you will be disappointed.
10123{_}2470{_}A moment ago you said you wished to do the right thing, at last.
10123{_}2471{_}Don't you know what that is?"
10123{_}2472{_}"Perhaps you will tell me," said Aunt Jane, curiously.
10123{_}2473{_}"With pleasure," returned Patsy.
10123{_}2474{_}"Mr. Bradley left you this property because he loved you, and love blinded him to all sense of justice.
10123{_}2475{_}Such an estate should not have passed into the hands of aliens because of a lover's whim.
10123{_}2476{_}He should have considered his own flesh and blood."
10123{_}2477{_}"There was no one but his sister, who at that time was not married and had no son," explained Aunt Jane, calmly.
10123{_}2478{_}"But he did not forget her and asked me to look after Katherine Bradley in case she or her heirs ever needed help.
10123{_}2479{_}I have done so.
10123{_}2480{_}When his mother died, I had the boy brought here, and he has lived here ever since."
10123{_}2481{_}"But the property ought to be his," said Patricia, earnestly.
10123{_}2482{_}"It would please me beyond measure to have you make your will in his favor, and you would be doing the right thing at last."
10123{_}2483{_}"I won't," said Aunt Jane, angrily.
10123{_}2484{_}"It would also be considerate and just to the memory of Mr. Bradley," continued the girl.
10123{_}2485{_}"What's going to became of Kenneth?"
10123{_}2486{_}"I have left him five thousand," said the woman.
10123{_}2487{_}"Not enough to educate him properly," replied Patsy, with a shake of her head.
10123{_}2488{_}"Why, the boy might become a famous artist, if he had good masters; and a person with an artistic temperament, such as his, should have enough money to be independent of his art."
10123{_}2489{_}Aunt Jane coughed, unsympathetically.
10123{_}2490{_}"The boy is nothing to me," she said.
10123{_}2491{_}"But he ought to have Elmhurst, at least," pleaded the girl.
10123{_}2492{_}"Won't you leave it to him, Aunt Jane?"
10123{_}2493{_}"No."
10123{_}2494{_}"Then do as you please," cried Patsy, flying angry in her turn.
10123{_}2495{_}"As a matter of justice, the place should never have been yours, and I won't accept a dollar of the money if I starve to death!"
10123{_}2496{_}"Think of your father," suggested Aunt Jane, cunningly.
10123{_}2497{_}"Ah, I've done that," said the girl, "and I know how many comforts I could buy for the dear Major.
10123{_}2498{_}Also I'd like to go to a girl's college, like Smith or Wellesley, and get a proper education.
10123{_}2499{_}But not with your money, Aunt Jane.
10123{_}2500{_}It would burn my fingers.
10123{_}2501{_}Always I would think that if you had not been hard and miserly this same money would have saved my mother's life.
10123{_}2502{_}No!
10123{_}2503{_}I loathe your money.
10123{_}2504{_}Keep it or throw it to the dogs, if you won't give it to the boy it belongs to.
10123{_}2505{_}But don't you dare to will your selfish hoard to me."
10123{_}2506{_}"Let us change the subject, Patricia."
10123{_}2507{_}"Will you change your will?"
10123{_}2508{_}"No.".
10123{_}2509{_}"Then I won't talk to you.
10123{_}2510{_}I'm angry and hurt, and if I stay here I'll say things I shall be sorry for."
10123{_}2511{_}With these words she marched out of the room, her cheeks flaming, and Aunt Jane looked after her with admiring eyes.
10123{_}2512{_}"She's right," she whispered to herself.
10123{_}2513{_}"It's just as I'd do under the same circumstances!"
10123{_}2514{_}This interview was but the beginning of a series that lasted during the next fortnight, during which time the invalid persisted in sending for Patricia and fighting the same fight over and over again.
10123{_}2515{_}Always the girl pleaded for Kenneth to inherit, and declared she would not accept the money and Elmhurst; and always Aunt Jane stubbornly refused to consider the boy and tried to tempt the girl with pictures of the luxury and pleasure that riches would bring her.
10123{_}2516{_}The interviews were generally short and spirited, however, and during the intervals Patsy associated more than ever with her cousins, both of whom grew really fond of her.
10123{_}2517{_}They fully believed Patricia when she declared she would never accept the inheritance, and although neither Beth nor Louise could understand such foolish sentimentality they were equally overjoyed at the girl's stand and the firmness with which she maintained it.
10123{_}2518{_}With Patsy out of the field it was quite possible the estate would be divided between her cousins, or even go entire to one or the other of them; and this hope constantly buoyed their spirits and filled their days with interest as they watched the fight between their aunt and their cousin.
10123{_}2519{_}Patricia never told them she was pleading so hard for the boy.
10123{_}2520{_}It would only pain her cousins and make them think she was disloyal to their interests; but she lost no opportunity when with her Aunt Jane of praising Kenneth and proving his ability, and finally she seemed to win her point.
10123{_}2521{_}Aunt Jane was really worn out with the constant squabbling with her favorite niece.
10123{_}2522{_}She had taken a turn for the worse, too, and began to decline rapidly.
10123{_}2523{_}So, her natural cunning and determination to have her own way enhanced by her illness, the woman decided to deceive Patricia and enjoy her few remaining days in peace.
10123{_}2524{_}"Suppose," she said to Mr. Watson, "my present will stands, and after my death the estate becomes the property of Patricia.
10123{_}2525{_}Can she refuse it?"
10123{_}2526{_}"Not legally," returned the lawyer.
10123{_}2527{_}"It would remain in her name, but under my control, during her minority.
10123{_}2528{_}When she became of age, however, she could transfer it as she might choose."
10123{_}2529{_}"By that time she will have gained more sense," declared Aunt Jane, much pleased with this aspect of the case, "and it isn't reasonable that having enjoyed a fortune for a time any girl would throw it away.
10123{_}2530{_}I'll stick to my point, Silas, but I'll try to make Patricia believe she has won me over."
10123{_}2531{_}Therefore, the very next time that the girl pleaded with her to make Kenneth her heir, she said, with a clever assumption of resignation:  "Very well, Patricia; you shall have your way.
10123{_}2532{_}My only desire, child, is to please you, as you well know, and if you long to see Kenneth the owner of Elmhurst I will have a new will drawn in his favor."
10123{_}2533{_}Patricia could scarcely believe her ears.
10123{_}2534{_}"Do you really mean it, aunt?"
10123{_}2535{_}she asked, flushing red with pleasure.
10123{_}2536{_}"I mean exactly what I say, and now let us cease all bickerings, my dear, and my few remaining days will be peaceful and happy."
10123{_}2537{_}Patricia thanked her aunt with eager words, and said, as indeed she felt, that she could almost love Aunt Jane for her final, if dilatory, act of justice.
10123{_}2538{_}Mr. Watson chanced to enter the room at that moment, and the girl cried out:  "Tell him, aunt!
10123{_}2539{_}Let him get the paper ready at once."
10123{_}2540{_}"There is no reason for haste," said Aunt Jane, meeting; the lawyer's questioning gaze with some embarrassment.
10123{_}2541{_}Silas Watson was an honorable and upright man, and his client's frequent doubtful methods had in past years met his severe censure.
10123{_}2542{_}Yet he had once promised his dead friend, Tom Bradley, that he would serve Jane Merrick faithfully.
10123{_}2543{_}He had striven to do so, bearing with her faults of character when he found that he could not correct them.
10123{_}2544{_}His influence over her had never been very strong, however, and he had learned that it was the most easy as well as satisfactory method to bow to her iron will.
10123{_}2545{_}Her recent questionings had prepared him for some act of duplicity, but he had by no means understood her present object, nor did she mean that he should.
10123{_}2546{_}So she answered his questioning look by saying:  "I have promised Patricia that you shall draw a new will, leaving all my estate to Kenneth Forbes, except for the bequests that are mentioned in the present paper."
10123{_}2547{_}The lawyer regarded her with amazement.
10123{_}2548{_}Then his brow darkened, for he thought she was playing with the girl, and was not sincere.
10123{_}2549{_}"Tell him to draw up the paper right away, aunt!"
10123{_}2550{_}begged Patricia, with sparkling eyes.
10123{_}2551{_}"As soon as you can, Silas," said the invalid.
10123{_}2552{_}"And, aunt, can't you spare a little more to Louise and Beth?
10123{_}2553{_}It would make them so happy."
10123{_}2554{_}"Double the amount I had allowed to each of them," the woman commanded her lawyer.
10123{_}2555{_}"Can it all be ready to sign tonight?"
10123{_}2556{_}asked Patsy, excitedly.
10123{_}2557{_}"I'll try, my dear," replied the old lawyer, gravely.
10123{_}2558{_}Then he turned to Jane Merrick.
10123{_}2559{_}"Are you in earnest?"
10123{_}2560{_}he asked.
10123{_}2561{_}Patsy's heart suddenly sank.
10123{_}2562{_}"Yes," was the reply.
10123{_}2563{_}"I am tired of opposing this child's wishes.
10123{_}2564{_}What do I care what becomes of my money, when I am gone?
10123{_}2565{_}All that I desire is to have my remaining days peaceful."
10123{_}2566{_}The girl spring forward and kissed her rapturously.
10123{_}2567{_}"They shall be, aunt!"
10123{_}2568{_}she cried.
10123{_}2569{_}"I promise it."
10123{_}2570{_}CHAPTER XX.
10123{_}2571{_}IN THE GARDEN.
10123{_}2572{_}From this hour Patsy devoted herself untiringly to Aunt Jane, and filled her days with as much sunshine as her merry ways and happy nature could confer.
10123{_}2573{_}Yet there was one thing that rendered her uneasy: the paper that Lawyer Watson had so promptly drawn had never yet been signed and witnessed.
10123{_}2574{_}Her aunt had allowed her to read it, saying she wished the girl to know she had acted in good faith, and Patsy had no fault at all to find with the document.
10123{_}2575{_}But Aunt Jane was tired, and deferred signing it that evening.
10123{_}2576{_}The next day no witnesses could be secured, and so another postponement followed, and upon one pretext or another the matter was put off until Patricia became suspicious.
10123{_}2577{_}Noting this, Aunt Jane decided to complete her act of deception.
10123{_}2578{_}She signed the will in the girl's presence, with Oscar and Susan to witness her signature.
10123{_}2579{_}Lawyer Watson was not present on this occasion, and as soon as Patsy had left her Miss Merrick tore off the signatures and burned them, wrote "void" in bold letters across the face of the paper, and then, it being rendered of no value, she enclosed it in a large yellow envelope, sealed it, and that evening handed the envelope to Mr. Watson with the request that it be not opened until after her death.
10123{_}2580{_}Patricia, in her delight, whispered to the lawyer that the paper was really signed, and he was well pleased and guarded the supposed treasure carefully.
10123{_}2581{_}The girl also took occasion to inform both Beth and Louise that a new will had been made in which they both profited largely, but she kept the secret of who the real heir was, and both her cousins grew to believe they would share equally in the entire property.
10123{_}2582{_}So now an air of harmony settled upon Elmhurst, and Uncle John joined the others in admiration of the girl who had conquered the stubbornness of her stern old aunt and proved herself so unselfish and true.
10123{_}2583{_}One morning Aunt Jane had Phibbs wheel her into her little garden, as usual, and busied herself examining the flowers and plants of which she had always been so fond.
10123{_}2584{_}"James has been neglecting his work, lately," she said, sharply, to her attendant.
10123{_}2585{_}"He's very queer, ma'am," replied old Martha, "ever since the young ladies an' Master John came to Elmhurst.
10123{_}2586{_}Strangers he never could abide, as you know, and he runs and hides himself as soon as he sees any of 'em about."
10123{_}2587{_}"Poor James!"
10123{_}2588{_}said Miss Merrick, recalling her old gardener's infirmity.
10123{_}2589{_}"But he must not neglect my flowers in this way, or they will be ruined."
10123{_}2590{_}"He isn't so afraid of Master John," went on Phibbs, reflectively, "as he is of the young ladies.
10123{_}2591{_}Sometimes Master John talks to James, in his quiet way, and I've noticed he listens to him quite respectively--like he always does to you, Miss Jane."
10123{_}2592{_}"Go and find James, and ask him to step here," commanded the mistress, "and then guard the opening in the hedge, and see that none of my nieces appear to bother him."
10123{_}2593{_}Phibbs obediently started upon her errand, and came upon James in the tool-house, at the end of the big garden.
10123{_}2594{_}He was working among his flower pots and seemed in a quieter mood than usual.
10123{_}2595{_}Phibbs delivered her message, and the gardener at once started to obey.
10123{_}2596{_}He crossed the garden unobserved and entered the little enclosure where Miss Jane's chair stood.
10123{_}2597{_}The invalid was leaning back on her cushions, but her eyes were wide open and staring.
10123{_}2598{_}"I've come, Miss," said James; and then, getting; no reply, he looked into her face.
10123{_}2599{_}A gleam of sunlight filtered through the bushes and fell aslant Jane Merrick's eyes; but not a lash quivered.
10123{_}2600{_}James gave a scream that rang through the air and silenced even the birds.
10123{_}2601{_}Then, shrieking like the madman he was, he bounded away through the hedge, sending old Martha whirling into a rose-bush, and fled as if a thousand fiends were at his heels.
10123{_}2602{_}John Merrick and Mr. Watson, who were not far off, aroused by the bloodcurdling screams, ran toward Aunt Jane's garden, and saw in a glance what had happened.
10123{_}2603{_}"Poor Jane," whispered the brother, bending over to tenderly close the staring eyes, "her fate has overtaken her unawares."
10123{_}2604{_}"Better so," said the lawyer, gently.
10123{_}2605{_}"She has found Peace at last."
10123{_}2606{_}Together they wheeled her back into her chamber, and called the women to care for their dead mistress.
10123{_}2607{_}CHAPTER XXI.
10123{_}2608{_}READING THE WILL.
10123{_}2609{_}Aunt Jane's funeral was extremely simple and quiet.
10123{_}2610{_}The woman had made no friends during her long residence in the neighborhood, having isolated herself at "the big house" and refused to communicate in any way with the families living near by.
10123{_}2611{_}Therefore, although her death undoubtedly aroused much interest and comment, no one cared to be present at the obsequies.
10123{_}2612{_}So the minister came from Elmwood, and being unable to say much that was good or bad of "the woman who had departed from this vale of tears," he confined his remarks to generalities and made them as brief as possible.
10123{_}2613{_}Then the body was borne to the little graveyard a mile away, followed by the state carriage, containing the three nieces and Kenneth; the drag with Silas Watson and Uncle John, the former driving; and then came the Elmhurst carryall with the servants.
10123{_}2614{_}James did not join these last; nor did he appear at the house after that dreadful scene in the garden.
10123{_}2615{_}He had a little room over the tool-house, which Jane Merrick had had prepared for him years ago, and here he locked himself in day and night, stealthily emerging but to secure the food Susan carried and placed before his door.
10123{_}2616{_}No one minded James much, for all the inmates of Elhurst were under severe and exciting strain in the days preceding the funeral.
10123{_}2617{_}The girls wept a little, but it was more on account of the solemnity following the shadow of death than for any great affection they bore their aunt.
10123{_}2618{_}Patsy, indeed, tried to deliver a tribute to Aunt Jane's memory; but it was not an emphatic success.
10123{_}2619{_}"I'm sure she had a good heart," said the girl, "and if she had lived more with her own family and cultivated her friends she would have been much less hard and selfish.
10123{_}2620{_}At the last, you know, she was quite gentle."
10123{_}2621{_}"I hadn't noticed it," remarked Beth.
10123{_}2622{_}"Oh, I did.
10123{_}2623{_}And she made a new will, after that awful one she told us of, and tried to be just and fair to all"  "I'm glad to hear that" said Louise.
10123{_}2624{_}"Tell us, Patsy, what does the will say?
10123{_}2625{_}You must know all about it."
10123{_}2626{_}"Mr. Watson is going to read it, after the funeral," replied the girl, "and then you will know as much about it as I do.
10123{_}2627{_}I mustn't tell secrets, my dear."
10123{_}2628{_}So Louise and Beth waited in much nervous excitement for the final realization of their hopes or fears, and during the drive to the cemetery there was little conversation in the state carriage.
10123{_}2629{_}Kenneth's sensitive nature was greatly affected by the death of the woman who had played so important a part in the brief story of his life, and the awe it inspired rendered him gloomy and silent.
10123{_}2630{_}Lawyer Watson had once warned him that Miss Merrick's death might make him an outcast, and he felt the insecurity of his present position.
10123{_}2631{_}But Patsy, believing he would soon know of his good fortune, watched him curiously during the ride, and beamed upon him as frequently as her own low spirits would permit.
10123{_}2632{_}"You know, Ken," she reminded him, "that whatever happens we are always to remain friends."
10123{_}2633{_}"Of course," replied the boy, briefly.
10123{_}2634{_}The girl had thrown aside her crutches, by this time, and planned to return to her work immediately after the funeral.
10123{_}2635{_}The brief services at the cemetery being concluded, the little cavalcade returned to Elmhurst, where luncheon was awaiting them.
10123{_}2636{_}Then Mr. Watson brought into the drawing room the tin box containing the important Elmhurst papers in his possession, and having requested all present to be seated he said:  "In order to clear up the uncertainty that at present exists concerning Miss Merrick's last will and testament, I will now proceed to read to you the document, which will afterward be properly probated according to law."
10123{_}2637{_}There was no need to request their attention.
10123{_}2638{_}An intense stillness pervaded the room.
10123{_}2639{_}The lawyer calmly unlocked the tin box and drew out the sealed yellow envelope which Miss Merrick had recently given him.
10123{_}2640{_}Patsy's heart was beating with eager expectancy.
10123{_}2641{_}She watched the lawyer break the seal, draw out the paper and then turn red and angry.
10123{_}2642{_}He hesitated a moment, and then thrust the useless document into its enclosure and cast it aside.
10123{_}2643{_}"Is anything wrong?"
10123{_}2644{_}asked the girl in a low whisper, which was yet distinctly heard by all.
